Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
6 min
The Concept of 'Awl in Inheritance Calculations
Explains the rule of 'awl from base 6 to 7, 8, 9, 10.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of 'awl to inheritance cases with base 6 and calculate the revised shares when the total prescribed shares exceed the base.

Core Idea
When fixed shares sum to more than six, the base increases proportionally — this is 'awl.

This passage introduces the crucial concept of 'awl (increase) in Hanafi inheritance calculations. When the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the base denominator, 'awl allows a proportional reduction so that each heir receives a reduced share. The focus here is on cases starting from base 6, which 'awl to 7, 8, 9, or 10. You will learn the rule, see two examples of 'awl to 7, and understand the companion proof underpinning this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base number (asl al-mas'alah)
When the heirs include combinations like half + third, half + sixth, or sixth + remainder, the base (LCM) is 6.
This is determined by the denominators of the prescribed shares: 1/2, 1/3, 1/6 -> LCM = 6.
2
Calculate the sum of prescribed shares as fractions of the base
Convert each share to a fraction with denominator 6, then sum the numerators.
Example: husband 1/2 = 3/6, two full sisters 2/3 = 4/6, sum = 7/6.
3
Detect if 'awl is needed
If the numerator sum exceeds the denominator (6), 'awl is required.
Here 7 > 6, so 'awl applies.
4
Apply 'awl by increasing the base
Set the new base equal to the numerator sum (7). Each heir's share becomes the original numerator over this new base.
Husband 3/7, two sisters 4/7. The original ratio is preserved.
5
Verify the result
Check that the sum of the new shares equals 1 (e.g., 3/7 + 4/7 = 7/7 = 1) and that the proportional reduction is correct.
The shares are now fractions of the estate that sum to the whole.

میت 6 عول 7

ایک حقیقی بہن 3
ایک باپ شریک بہن 1
Chapter on Calculation of Inheritances. And if there is a sixth and a remainder, or a half and a third, or a half and a sixth, then its origin is from six, and it increases ('awl) to seven, eight, nine, and ten. And if there is a sixth and a remainder, or a half and a third, or a half and a sixth, then the base of the problem is from six. It will increase to seven, eight, nine, and ten. If the recipients are a sixth and a remainder, the problem proceeds from six. Sometimes the recipients are within six shares, but sometimes there are so many that when their shares are added, they exceed six. Now the problem is made from six and the shares become seven; this excess of shares over the base is called 'awl. The lexical meaning of 'awl is inclining and oppression. Since the remaining heirs will now suffer a loss, this type of problem is named 'awl. Forms of 'awl: The case where the base problem proceeds from six and the shares become seven is as follows: The deceased left a husband and two full sisters. In this, the husband gets half because there is no child, and the two full sisters get two-thirds, so the problem proceeds from six. The problem: Deceased 6, 'awl 7; Husband 3; Two full sisters 4. So the husband gets half, i.e., three, and the two sisters get two-thirds, i.e., four out of six. Their total becomes seven, so 'awl is from seven. The proof for 'awl is this athar: From Ibrahim, that 'Ali, 'Abdullah, and Zaid used to practice 'awl (al-Maghribi, Ibn Abi Shayba, etc.). This athar indicates that these companions practiced 'awl. Second example of 'awl to seven: The deceased left a husband, one full sister, and one paternal sister. Since there is no child, the husband gets half, one full sister gets half, and to complete two-thirds, the paternal sister is given one-sixth. So the problem proceeds from six and the total becomes seven, which is called 'awl. Deceased 6, 'awl 7; Husband 3; One full sister 3; One paternal sister 1.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the concept of 'awl (increase) in inheritance calculations. The author explains that when the prescribed shares of heirs sum to more than the base number (asl al-mas'alah) of 6, the base is increased proportionally through 'awl. The base number 6 is used when the heirs include combinations like a sixth and a remainder, a half and a third, or a half and a sixth. The 'awl can be to 7, 8, 9, or 10 depending on the shares. Two examples illustrate 'awl to 7: first, a husband (half = 3/6) and two full sisters (two-thirds = 4/6) together make 7/6; second, a husband (half = 3/6), a full sister (half = 3/6), and a paternal sister (one-sixth = 1/6) also make 7/6. The author provides a proof from the practices of the companions 'Ali, 'Abdullah, and Zaid (may Allah be pleased with them), indicating that 'awl was accepted by early authorities. The lexical meaning of 'awl is explained as 'inclining' or 'oppression' because the shares of heirs are reduced proportionally.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): The process of increasing the base number (asl al-mas'alah) when the sum of prescribed shares exceeds it, so that each heir's share is proportionally reduced.
فريضه (faridah): An inheritance case or the prescribed shares.
اصل مسئلہ (asl al-mas'alah): The base denominator used to calculate shares; the least common multiple of the share denominators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first example of 'awl to 7, what are the shares of the husband and two full sisters after 'awl?
A) Husband 3/7, two full sisters 4/7
B) Husband 1/2, two full sisters 2/3
C) Husband 3/6, two full sisters 4/6
D) Husband 1/3, two full sisters 2/3

Key Takeaway
'Awl is the proportional increase of the base number when fixed shares exceed the base, ensuring equitable distribution.

Faraid — Inheritance

Concept and Evidence of 'Awl in Hanafi Faraid
Introduces 'awl with a definition, first example, and an athar proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'awl, explain its necessity when prescribed shares exceed the estate, and cite the Hanafi proof from the Companions Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid.

Core Idea
When prescribed shares exceed the estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each share—proven by the practice of Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid.

Inheritance calculations become problematic when the sum of prescribed shares (furud) exceeds the total estate. The Hanafi school resolves this through 'awl, a proportional reduction of every share. This lesson introduces the concept, walks through the first example, and examines the athar (report) that provides the proof for this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Observe that in the first example, the husband's half (50) plus two full sisters' two-thirds (66.66) totals 116.66, exceeding the estate of 100. This is the situation that requires 'awl.
The prescribed shares are fixed; the estate is fixed; mathematical conflict arises.
2
Define 'awl
'Awl is the proportional reduction of each heir's share so that the total fits within the estate. The denominator is increased from the original (e.g., 6) to the sum of share units (e.g., 7, 8, etc.).
The word 'awl literally means 'to incline' or 'to rise'—here it refers to the increase in the denominator.
3
Work through the first example
For husband (1/2 = 3/6) and two full sisters (2/3 = 4/6), the shares total 7/6. Convert to denominator 7: husband gets 3/7 of the estate, sisters get 4/7. The numbers given in the source confirm this reduction.
The modern calculator method divides 100 by 116.66 and multiplies each heir's original amount.
4
Analyze the proof (athar)
The source quotes Ibrahim al-Nakha'i reporting that Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit practiced 'awl. This establishes a binding precedent from major Companions.
The chain is from Ibrahim to these Companions; although the report is ahad, its meaning is qat'i due to widespread acceptance.
5
Recognize the consensus
The Hanafi school follows the majority Companion practice. The minority view (Ibn Abbas) rejecting 'awl is outweighed by the stronger proof of practice and later consensus.
This will be explored further in lesson 3.

مجموعه
اس مسئلے میں شوہر کو سو کا آدھا 50 دیا، باپ شریک بہن کو سو کی دو تہائی 66.66 دیا۔ اور ماں کو چھٹا حصہ 16.66 دیا۔ سب کا مجموعہ 133.32 ہو گیا۔ جو سو سے زیادہ ہے اور عول ہے۔ چونکہ سو ہی سے حساب رکھنا ہے اس لئے 133.32 سے 100 کو تقسیم کر دیا تو 0.7500 آیا جو ایک حصے والے کو ملے گا۔ اب اس کو 50 میں ضرب دیں 37.50-0.7500x50 ہوگا جو شوہر کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور 66.66 کو 0.7500 میں ضرب دیا تو 49.99 ہوا جو بہن کو دیا۔ اور 16.49 کو 0.7500 سے ضرب دیا تو 12.49 ہوا جو ماں کو دے
Chapter on the calculation of inheritances. Six, and it 'awl to seven, eight, nine, and ten. In this case, the husband was given half of a hundred, 50. And the two full sisters were given two-thirds of a hundred, 66.66. Adding both gives 116.66, one hundred sixteen point sixty-six, which exceeds one hundred. This is called 'awl. However, we must keep the shares within a hundred, so we divided 116.66 by 100, resulting in 0.8571. That is, one share gets this. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85. This becomes the husband's share. And multiply 66.66 by 0.8571: 66.66 × 0.8571 = 57.13. This is given to the two sisters. Their total is 99.98, which is close to one hundred. This is actually the correct amount, but there is a slight deficiency of one new paisa in the calculator's calculation. Now the husband gets 42.85 dirhams out of 100 dirhams, and the sister gets 57.13 dirhams out of 100 dirhams. The proof for 'awl is this athar: From Ibrahim, from Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid: they applied 'awl to the faridah. (Ref: Mushaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bayhaqi). This athar indicates that these Companions practiced 'awl. Second example of 'awl to seven: The deceased left a husband, one full sister, and one consanguine sister. Since he left no children, the husband gets half. The full sister gets half. The consanguine sister is given one-sixth to complete two-thirds. Therefore, the case is based on six, and the total becomes seven, which is called 'awl. The case is as follows: Deceased 6, 'awl 7: Husband 3, full sister 3, consanguine sister 1. The calculator calculation would be: Deceased 100, 'awl 116.66, after 'awl one share 0.8571 = 100/116.66. Husband: 50, after 'awl gets 42.85. Full sister: 50, after 'awl gets 42.85. Consanguine sister: 16.66, after 'awl gets 14.27. Total 99.97. Footnote: (a) Ibrahim says that Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid practiced 'awl. Method of 'awl. [Page 461] In this case, the husband was given half of 100, 50. The sister was given half of 100, 50. The consanguine sister was given one-sixth, 16.66. The total of all is 116.66, which is called 'awl. Since the calculation must be from 100, we divide 100 by 116.66, giving 0.8571, which is the share of each unit. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85, which is the share of the husband and also the full sister. Give them to both. Multiply 16.66 by 0.8571, giving 14.27. Give this to the consanguine sister whose share was one-sixth. The total is 99.97, which is close to 100. So the husband gets 42.85 dirhams, the full sister gets 42.85 dirhams, and the consanguine sister gets 14.27 dirhams out of 100 dirhams. Example of 'awl to eight: The deceased left a husband, two consanguine sisters, and a mother. Since there are no children, the husband gets half. The two consanguine sisters get two-thirds. The mother gets one-sixth. Therefore, the case is based on six, and the total becomes eight. The case is as follows: Deceased 6, 'awl 8: Husband 3, two consanguine sisters 4, mother 1. The calculator calculation: Deceased 100, 'awl 133.32, after 'awl one share 0.7500 = 100/133.33. Husband: 50, after 'awl gets 37.50. Two consanguine sisters: 66.66, after 'awl get 49.99. Mother: 16.66, after 'awl gets 12.49. Total 99.98. Conclusion: In this case, the husband was given half of 100, 50; the two consanguine sisters were given two-thirds of 100, 66.66; the mother was given one-sixth, 16.66. The total became 133.32, which exceeds 100, and that is 'awl. Since the calculation must be from 100, we divide 100 by 133.32, giving 0.7500, which is the share of each unit. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.7500 = 37.50, which is the husband's share. Multiply 66.66 by 0.7500: 49.99, given to the sisters. Multiply 16.66 by 0.7500: 12.49, given to the mother.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains the concept of 'awl in inheritance calculations. 'Awl occurs when the sum of the prescribed shares (furud) exceeds the total estate, requiring proportional reduction. The author provides three examples: 'awl to 7, 'awl to 8, and mentions 'awl to 9 and 10. For each, the method is to convert the original denominator (6) to the 'awl denominator (7 or 8) and then calculate shares proportionally. The modern calculator approach using percentage reduction is also shown. The proof offered is an athar (tradition) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit practiced 'awl. This establishes the practice as accepted by the early community. In the Hanafi school, 'awl is fully accepted, unlike the view of some early scholars like Ibn Abbas who rejected it. The method ensures each heir receives a reduced share proportional to their original entitlement. The examples illustrate cases with husband, full sisters, consanguine sisters, and mother. The Hanafi position is that 'awl is necessary by necessity (darurah) when the shares exceed the estate, and it is applied based on the consensus of the Companions.

Key Terms
العول (al-'awl): Proportional reduction of the prescribed shares when their total exceeds the estate, so that each heir receives a reduced share proportionally.
فريضة (farīḍah): An inheritance case; also refers to the prescribed share of an heir.
حقیقی بہن (ḥaqīqī bahn): A full sister (germane sister) who shares both parents with the deceased.
باپ شریک بہن (bāp sharīk bahn): A consanguine sister (paternal half-sister), sharing the same father but a different mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct proof for 'awl?
A) A Quranic verse explicitly commanding 'awl.
B) A hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) stating the rule.
C) An athar (report) that the Companions Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit practiced 'awl.
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone.

Key Takeaway
'Awl is a proportional reduction of shares necessary when prescribed shares exceed the estate, supported by Companion practice and Hanafi consensus.

Calculating 'Awl: From Six to Seven, Eight, and Beyond
Provides worked examples of 'awl calculations up to denominator 8, with both traditional and modern methods.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compute 'awl adjustments for inheritance cases using both the traditional denominator method and the modern percentage reduction method.

Core Idea
'Awl calculations raise the base denominator from 6 to 7, 8, 9, or 10, reducing each share proportionally—mastering this ensures accurate distribution.

This lesson provides hands-on practice with 'awl calculations. We will walk through three examples from the source, each illustrating a different scenario: 'awl to 7, 'awl to 8, and an introduction to higher 'awls. By the end, you will be able to apply the method confidently.

Guided Path
1
Review the first example: 'awl to 7 (husband + two full sisters)
Original shares: husband 1/2 (3/6), two full sisters 2/3 (4/6). Sum = 7/6. New denominator = 7. Husband gets 3/7, sisters get 4/7. Confirm with the modern method: total original units = 116.66; reduction factor = 100/116.66 = 0.8571.
This case shows the basic 'awl to 7.
2
Work through the second example: 'awl to 7 (husband + full sister + consanguine sister)
Shares: husband 1/2 (3/6), full sister 1/2 (3/6), consanguine sister 1/6 (1/6). Sum = 7/6. New denominator = 7. Husband gets 3/7, full sister gets 3/7, consanguine sister gets 1/7. Modern: reduction factor = 0.8571.
Note that the consanguine sister's share is 1/6, but after 'awl it reduces to 1/7.
3
Work through the third example: 'awl to 8 (husband + two consanguine sisters + mother)
Shares: husband 1/2 (3/6), two consanguine sisters 2/3 (4/6), mother 1/6 (1/6). Sum = 8/6. New denominator = 8. Husband gets 3/8, sisters get 4/8, mother gets 1/8. Reduction factor = 100/133.32 = 0.7500.
This case increases denominator to 8.
4
Understand the general method
Always start with denominator 6 (or the appropriate base). Sum the share units. The new denominator is that sum. Each heir's new fraction = their share units / sum. Multiply by the estate to get actual shares.
The modern percentage method achieves the same result by dividing 100 by the total original percentage.

Chapter on the calculation of inheritances. Six, and it 'awl to seven, eight, nine, and ten. In this case, the husband was given half of a hundred, 50. And the two full sisters were given two-thirds of a hundred, 66.66. Adding both gives 116.66, one hundred sixteen point sixty-six, which exceeds one hundred. This is called 'awl. However, we must keep the shares within a hundred, so we divided 116.66 by 100, resulting in 0.8571. That is, one share gets this. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85. This becomes the husband's share. And multiply 66.66 by 0.8571: 66.66 × 0.8571 = 57.13. This is given to the two sisters. Their total is 99.98, which is close to one hundred. This is actually the correct amount, but there is a slight deficiency of one new paisa in the calculator's calculation. Now the husband gets 42.85 dirhams out of 100 dirhams, and the sister gets 57.13 dirhams out of 100 dirhams. The proof for 'awl is this athar: From Ibrahim, from Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid: they applied 'awl to the faridah. (Ref: Mushaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bayhaqi). This athar indicates that these Companions practiced 'awl. Second example of 'awl to seven: The deceased left a husband, one full sister, and one consanguine sister. Since he left no children, the husband gets half. The full sister gets half. The consanguine sister is given one-sixth to complete two-thirds. Therefore, the case is based on six, and the total becomes seven, which is called 'awl. The case is as follows: Deceased 6, 'awl 7: Husband 3, full sister 3, consanguine sister 1. The calculator calculation would be: Deceased 100, 'awl 116.66, after 'awl one share 0.8571 = 100/116.66. Husband: 50, after 'awl gets 42.85. Full sister: 50, after 'awl gets 42.85. Consanguine sister: 16.66, after 'awl gets 14.27. Total 99.97. Footnote: (a) Ibrahim says that Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid practiced 'awl. Method of 'awl. [Page 461] In this case, the husband was given half of 100, 50. The sister was given half of 100, 50. The consanguine sister was given one-sixth, 16.66. The total of all is 116.66, which is called 'awl. Since the calculation must be from 100, we divide 100 by 116.66, giving 0.8571, which is the share of each unit. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85, which is the share of the husband and also the full sister. Give them to both. Multiply 16.66 by 0.8571, giving 14.27. Give this to the consanguine sister whose share was one-sixth. The total is 99.97, which is close to 100. So the husband gets 42.85 dirhams, the full sister gets 42.85 dirhams, and the consanguine sister gets 14.27 dirhams out of 100 dirhams. Example of 'awl to eight: The deceased left a husband, two consanguine sisters, and a mother. Since there are no children, the husband gets half. The two consanguine sisters get two-thirds. The mother gets one-sixth. Therefore, the case is based on six, and the total becomes eight. The case is as follows: Deceased 6, 'awl 8: Husband 3, two consanguine sisters 4, mother 1. Mother: 16.66, after 'awl gets 12.49. Total 99.98. The 'Awl Controversy: From Ibn Abbas's Opposition to Hanafi Consensus
Discusses the legal dispute over 'awl, presenting the minority rejection and the Hanafi response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the minority view of Ibn Abbas rejecting 'awl and evaluate the Hanafi response based on Companion practice and consensus.

Core Idea
Ibn Abbas argued shares should not be reduced, but the majority Companions including Ali and Zaid practiced 'awl, forming the basis of the Hanafi position.

While 'awl is standard in Hanafi faraid, it was not without early opposition. This lesson explores the scholarly disagreement between the majority Companions who accepted 'awl and the minority view attributed to Ibn Abbas. Understanding this ikhtilaf strengthens your grasp of Hanafi legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Present the minority view
Ibn Abbas (and others) held that the Quranic shares are fixed and should not be reduced. In cases of excess, the deficiency should be placed on the 'asabah (residual heirs) or the estate should be divided according to the shares without reduction, meaning some heirs might not receive their full prescribed share but the shares are not proportionally reduced.
This view is based on a literal reading of the Quranic verses.
2
Present the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites the athar: Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit practiced 'awl. This practice from major Companions is considered a binding interpretation of the Quranic injunctions.
The athar is the same proof used for the ruling.
3
Analyze the strength of each position
The majority view is supported by the practice of three prominent Companions and later consensus (ijma) of the ummah. The minority view rests on a literal reading but lacks Companion consensus.
The Hanafi school weights the precedent of Companion practice (qaul al-sahabi) heavily.
4
Understand the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the majority view because the proof from practice is stronger and more consistent with the need for practical distribution. The minority view is acknowledged but not operative.
The mufta-bihi position is the acceptance of 'awl.

اس مسئلے میں شوہر کو سو میں سے آدھا 50 دیا۔ بہن کو سو میں سے آدھا 50 دیا۔ اور باپ شریک بہن کو چھٹا حصہ 16.66 دیا ۔ ان سب کا مجموعہ 116.66 ہوا۔ جس کو عول کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ سو سے ہی حساب رکھنا ہے۔ اس لئے 116.66 کو 100 میں تقسیم دیں تو 0.8571 نکلے گا جو ایک حصہ والے کا حصہ ہے۔ اس کو 50 میں ضرب دیں 50 × 0.8571 =42.85 ہوگا جو شوہر کا بھی حصہ ہے اور حقیقی بہن کا بھی حصہ ہے۔ یہ دونوں کو دے دیں۔ اور 16.66 کو 0.8571 میں ضرب دیں تو 14.27 نکلے گا۔ یہ باپ شریک بہن کو دے دیں جس کا چھٹا حصہ تھا۔ اور سب کا مجموعہ 99.97 ہوگا جو سو کے قریب ہے۔ تو اب شوہر کو سو درہم میں سے 42.85 درہم حقیقی بہن کو سو درہم میں سے 42.85 درہم ملے گا ۔ اور باپ شریک بہن کو سو درہم میں سے 14.27 درہم ملے گا۔ آٹھ تک عول ہونے کی مثال : میت نے شوہر ، دو باپ شریک بہن اور ماں چھوڑی، چونکہ اولاد نہیں ہے اس لئے شوہر کو آدھا ملے گا۔ اور باپ شریک دو بہنیں ہیں اس لئے ان کو دو تہائی ملے گی۔ اور ماں کو چھٹا ملے گا۔ اس لئے مسئلہ چھ سے چلے گا۔ سب حصوں کا مجموعہ آٹھ ہوگا۔

اس مسئلے میں شوہر کو سو کا آدھا 50 دیا، باپ شریک بہن کو سو کی دو تہائی 66.66 دیا۔ اور ماں کو چھٹا حصہ 16.66 دیا۔ سب کا مجموعہ 133.32 ہو گیا۔ جو سو سے زیادہ ہے اور عول ہے۔ چونکہ سو ہی سے حساب رکھنا ہے اس لئے 133.32 سے 100 کو تقسیم کر دیا تو 0.7500 آیا جو ایک حصے والے کو ملے گا۔ اب اس کو 50 میں ضرب دیں 37.50-0.7500x50 ہوگا جو شوہر کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور 66.66 کو 0.7500 میں ضرب دیا تو 49.99 ہوا جو بہن کو دیا۔ اور 16.49 کو 0.7500 سے ضرب دیا تو 12.49 ہوا جو ماں کو دے
Chapter on the calculation of inheritances. Six, and it 'awl to seven, eight, nine, and ten. In this case, the husband was given half of a hundred, 50. And the two full sisters were given two-thirds of a hundred, 66.66. Adding both gives 116.66, one hundred sixteen point sixty-six, which exceeds one hundred. This is called 'awl. However, we must keep the shares within a hundred, so we divided 116.66 by 100, resulting in 0.8571. That is, one share gets this. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85. This becomes the husband's share. And multiply 66.66 by 0.8571: 66.66 × 0.8571 = 57.13. This is given to the two sisters. Their total is 99.98, which is close to one hundred. This is actually the correct amount, but there is a slight deficiency of one new paisa in the calculator's calculation. Now the husband gets 42.85 dirhams out of 100 dirhams, and the sister gets 57.13 dirhams out of 100 dirhams. The proof for 'awl is this athar: From Ibrahim, from Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid: they applied 'awl to the faridah. (Ref: Mushaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Bayhaqi). This athar indicates that these Companions practiced 'awl. Second example of 'awl to seven: The deceased left a husband, one full sister, and one consanguine sister. Since he left no children, the husband gets half. The full sister gets half. The consanguine sister is given one-sixth to complete two-thirds. Therefore, the case is based on six, and the total becomes seven, which is called 'awl. The case is as follows: Deceased 6, 'awl 7: Husband 3, full sister 3, consanguine sister 1. The calculator calculation would be: Deceased 100, 'awl 116.66, after 'awl one share 0.8571 = 100/116.66. Husband: 50, after 'awl gets 42.85. Full sister: 50, after 'awl gets 42.85. Consanguine sister: 16.66, after 'awl gets 14.27. Total 99.97. Footnote: (a) Ibrahim says that Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid practiced 'awl. Method of 'awl. [Page 461] In this case, the husband was given half of 100, 50. The sister was given half of 100, 50. The consanguine sister was given one-sixth, 16.66. The total of all is 116.66, which is called 'awl. Since the calculation must be from 100, we divide 100 by 116.66, giving 0.8571, which is the share of each unit. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85, which is the share of the husband and also the full sister. Give them to both. Multiply 16.66 by 0.8571, giving 14.27. Give this to the consanguine sister whose share was one-sixth. The total is 99.97, which is close to 100. So the husband gets 42.85 dirhams, the full sister gets 42.85 dirhams, and the consanguine sister gets 14.27 dirhams out of 100 dirhams. Example of 'awl to eight: The deceased left a husband, two consanguine sisters, and a mother. Since there are no children, the husband gets half. The two consanguine sisters get two-thirds. The mother gets one-sixth. Therefore, the case is based on six, and the total becomes eight. The case is as follows: Deceased 6, 'awl 8: Husband 3, two consanguine sisters 4, mother 1. The calculator calculation: Deceased 100, 'awl 133.32, after 'awl one share 0.7500 = 100/133.33. Husband: 50, after 'awl gets 37.50. Two consanguine sisters: 66.66, after 'awl get 49.99. Mother: 16.66, after 'awl gets 12.49. Total 99.98. Conclusion: In this case, the husband was given half of 100, 50; the two consanguine sisters were given two-thirds of 100, 66.66; the mother was given one-sixth, 16.66. The total became 133.32, which exceeds 100, and that is 'awl. Since the calculation must be from 100, we divide 100 by 133.32, giving 0.7500, which is the share of each unit. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.7500 = 37.50, which is the husband's share. Multiply 66.66 by 0.7500: 49.99, given to the sisters. Multiply 16.66 by 0.7500: 12.49, given to the mother.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains the concept of 'awl in inheritance calculations. 'Awl occurs when the sum of the prescribed shares (furud) exceeds the total estate, requiring proportional reduction. The author provides three examples: 'awl to 7, 'awl to 8, and mentions 'awl to 9 and 10. For each, the method is to convert the original denominator (6) to the 'awl denominator (7 or 8) and then calculate shares proportionally. The modern calculator approach using percentage reduction is also shown. The proof offered is an athar (tradition) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that the Companions Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit practiced 'awl. This establishes the practice as accepted by the early community. In the Hanafi school, 'awl is fully accepted, unlike the view of some early scholars like Ibn Abbas who rejected it. The method ensures each heir receives a reduced share proportional to their original entitlement. The examples illustrate cases with husband, full sisters, consanguine sisters, and mother. The Hanafi position is that 'awl is necessary by necessity (darurah) when the shares exceed the estate, and it is applied based on the consensus of the Companions.

Key Terms
العول (al-'awl): Proportional reduction of shares when total exceeds estate.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars, a source of law.
خلاف (ikhtilaf): Scholarly disagreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who among the early scholars is most famously associated with rejecting 'awl?
A) Imam Abu Hanifa
B) Imam Shafi'i
C) Ibn Abbas
D) Zaid ibn Thabit

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi acceptance of 'awl is based on the practice of the majority of Companions, which outweighs the literal reading of Ibn Abbas.

Calculating 'Awl with Husband, Full Sister, and Consanguine Sister
Example of 'awl with three heirs and calculator method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the adjusted inheritance shares when the prescribed shares exceed the estate using the 'awl method, applying the reduction factor to each heir proportionally.

Core Idea
When shares exceed the estate, 'awl reduces each share proportionally, preserving the prescribed ratios.

In this lesson, we examine a classic fara'id scenario: a husband, a full sister, and a consanguine sister. Their combined Quranic shares total 7/6, exceeding the estate. The Hanafi solution is 'awl—proportional reduction. We will walk through the calculation step by step, including a practical method using 100 as a base for clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify heirs and prescribed shares
List the heirs: husband (1/2), full sister (1/2), consanguine sister (1/6). These are Quranic fard shares.
These shares apply when there are no children, father, or brothers to change the shares.
2
Sum the shares and detect excess
Add the shares: 1/2 + 1/2 + 1/6 = 7/6. Since 7/6 > 1, the estate is insufficient, requiring 'awl.
The total exceeds the whole estate by 1/6.
3
Convert to common denominator
The least common multiple of denominators (2,2,6) is 6. Shares become 3/6 (husband), 3/6 (full sister), 1/6 (consanguine sister). Sum = 7/6.
This step shows the excess clearly as 7/6.
4
Adjust denominator (apply 'awl)
Increase the base denominator from 6 to 7 to absorb the surplus. Now each share is expressed as a fraction of 7: husband 3/7, full sister 3/7, consanguine sister 1/7.
The estate is now divided into 7 equal parts instead of 6.
5
Calculate final shares
If the estate is 100 dirhams, multiply each fraction by 100: husband 42.85, full sister 42.85, consanguine sister 14.27. Summing gives ~100.
The calculator method: first compute each prescribed share as if the estate were 100, then multiply by reduction factor 100/116.66 ≈ 0.8571.

Source Text

باب حساب الفرائض

اس مسئلے میں شوہر کو سو میں سے آدھا 50 دیا۔ بہن کو سو میں سے آدھا 50 دیا۔ اور باپ شریک بہن کو چھٹا حصہ 16.66 دیا ۔ ان سب کا مجموعہ 116.66 ہوا۔ جس کو عول کہتے ہیں۔ چونکہ سو سے ہی حساب رکھنا ہے۔ اس لئے 116.66 کو 100 میں تقسیم دیں تو 0.8571 نکلے گا جو ایک حصہ والے کا حصہ ہے۔ اس کو 50 میں ضرب دیں 50 × 0.8571 =42.85 ہوگا جو شوہر کا بھی حصہ ہے اور حقیقی بہن کا بھی حصہ ہے۔ یہ دونوں کو دے دیں۔ اور 16.66 کو 0.8571 میں ضرب دیں تو 14.27 نکلے گا۔ یہ باپ شریک بہن کو دے دیں جس کا چھٹا حصہ تھا۔ اور سب کا مجموعہ 99.97 ہوگا جو سو کے قریب ہے۔ تو اب شوہر کو سو درہم میں سے 42.85 درہم حقیقی بہن کو سو درہم میں سے 42.85 درہم ملے گا ۔ اور باپ شریک بہن کو سو درہم میں سے 14.27 درہم ملے گا۔
Chapter of Calculation of Inheritance. In this case, the husband is given half of a hundred, 50. The sister is given half of a hundred, 50. And the consanguine sister is given a sixth share, 16.66. The total of all these is 116.66, which is called 'awal. Since the calculation must be based on a hundred, we divide 100 by 116.66, giving 0.8571, which is the share of each unit. Multiply it by 50: 50 × 0.8571 = 42.85, which is the share of both the husband and the full sister. Give these to both. Multiply 16.66 by 0.8571, giving 14.27. Give this to the consanguine sister, who had a sixth share. The total of all is 99.97, which is approximately a hundred. So now the husband receives 42.85 dirhams out of a hundred dirhams, the full sister receives 42.85 dirhams out of a hundred dirhams, and the consanguine sister receives 14.27 dirhams out of a hundred dirhams.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage presents a worked example of 'awl (proportional reduction) in inheritance distribution. The heirs are: a husband (entitled to 1/2), a full sister (entitled to 1/2), and a consanguine sister (entitled to 1/6). The prescribed shares sum to 7/6, exceeding the estate. To resolve this, the author uses a practical method: set the estate as 100 units, then calculate the reducing factor (100/116.66). Each heir's share is multiplied by this factor to obtain the adjusted distribution. This method avoids fractional complexities and yields the correct proportionate shares: husband and full sister each get 42.85%, consanguine sister gets 14.27%.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of prescribed shares when they exceed the estate
فرائض (fara'id): Inheritance shares prescribed in Quran and Sunnah

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 116.66
C) 133.32
D) 149.99

Key Takeaway

Awl to Eight: Husband, Two Consanguine Sisters, Mother
Example of 'awl with four heirs totaling eight-sixths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the estate distribution using 'awl when the total prescribed shares exceed the estate, specifically for the heirs: husband (1/2), two consanguine sisters (2/3), and mother (1/6).

Core Idea
When shares exceed the estate, the denominator increases proportionally, keeping the fractional shares unchanged.

In this lesson, we work through a classic 'awl case where a deceased leaves a husband, two consanguine sisters, and a mother. The prescribed shares sum to more than the full estate (8/6), triggering the 'awl procedure. By increasing the denominator from 6 to 8, each heir's fraction is preserved but the actual pay-out is proportionally reduced. Understanding this mechanism is essential for correctly dividing estates when the quotas exceed the available pool.

Guided Path
1
List the heirs and their prescribed shares
Identify each heir and the fixed share they are entitled to. Husband: 1/2 (because no children). Two consanguine sisters: 2/3 (because no father/brother). Mother: 1/6 (because the deceased has siblings but no children or father).
These shares are from the Quran and Sunnah.
2
Find the common denominator (asl al-masalah)
Convert all shares to a common base. The denominators are 2, 3, and 6; their LCM is 6. So husband = 3/6, sisters = 4/6, mother = 1/6.
The base number is 6.
3
Sum the shares and detect 'awl
Add the numerators: 3 + 4 + 1 = 8. The sum (8/6) exceeds 1, so the estate must be divided into 8 parts instead of 6. This is 'awl.
'Awl is required when total shares > estate.
4
Calculate the reducing factor
Set the estate as 100 units. The original share values: husband = 50, sisters = 66.66, mother = 16.66 (sum 133.32). The factor = 100 / 133.32 ≈ 0.75.
The factor rounds the distribution proportionally.
5
Apply the factor to each share
Multiply each original share by 0.75: husband 37.50, sisters 49.99 (approx. 25 each), mother 12.49. Total ≈ 99.98 (close to 100 due to rounding).
The exact fractions are husband 3/8, sisters 4/8 (each 2/8), mother 1/8.

Example of 'awl up to eight: The deceased left husband, two consanguine sisters, and mother. Since there are no children, the husband gets half. The two consanguine sisters get two-thirds. The mother gets one-sixth. So the problem works from six. The total of all shares is eight. The problem is set up as: Deceased 6, 'awl 8. Husband, two consanguine sisters, mother. The method of 'awl: 1, 4, 3. The calculator calculation is as follows: Deceased 100, 'awl 133.32. Husband. After 'awl each share 0.7500 = 100 divided by 133.33. Two consanguine sisters, mother. 16.66, 12.49, 66.66, 49.99. 16.66 x 0.7500 = 12.49, 66.66 x 0.7500 = 49.99, 50 x 0.7500 = 37.50, total 99.98. 50, 37.50. After 'awl mother gets, after 'awl two sisters get, after 'awl husband gets. Total. In this case, the husband is given half of a hundred, 50; the consanguine sisters two-thirds of a hundred, 66.66; and the mother a sixth share, 16.66. Their total became 133.32, which exceeds a hundred and is 'awl. Since the calculation is based on a hundred, divide 100 by 133.32, giving 0.7500, which is what one unit receives. Multiply it by 50: 37.50, which is the husband's share. Multiply 66.66 by 0.7500, giving 49.99, which is given to the sisters. Multiply 16.49 by 0.7500, giving 12.49, which is given to the mother. And the total of all is 99.98, which is approximately a hundred.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage presents an example of 'awl where the estate is divided among husband (1/2), two consanguine sisters (2/3), and mother (1/6). The sum of shares in sixths is 8/6, so the denominator is increased from 6 to 8. Using the practical calculator method with a base of 100, the reducing factor is 100/133.32 = 0.75. Each prescribed share is multiplied by this factor to yield the actual distribution: husband gets 37.50%, the two sisters collectively get 49.99% (i.e., approximately 25% each), and mother gets 12.49%. The slight rounding gives a total of 99.98%.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): Proportional increase of denominator to distribute shares exceeding estate

D) 0.5000

Key Takeaway
When shares exceed the estate, 'awl increases the denominator proportionally, preserving the fractional shares and ensuring a fair, proportional reduction for all heirs.

‘Awl to Nine: Husband, Consanguine and Uterine Sisters
Worked example of ‘awl with five heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares when a husband, two consanguine sisters, and two uterine sisters survive, applying ‘awl to proportionally reduce the shares.

Core Idea
When prescribed shares exceed the estate, increase the denominator and reduce each share proportionally — ‘awl ensures justice.

This passage works through a practical faraid case where five heirs (husband, two consanguine sisters, two uterine sisters) have prescribed fractions that sum to more than the whole estate. The classical method raises the base denominator from 6 to 9, and the modern method uses a scaling factor to distribute the estate exactly. Understanding this example will equip you to handle any ‘awl scenario.

Guided Path
1
List all surviving heirs and their prescribed shares
Identify the heirs: husband (1/2), two consanguine sisters (2/3), two uterine sisters (1/3). Note that no children or father exist, so these shares apply.
2
Convert shares to a common denominator (asl al-masalah)
The denominators are 2, 3, 3. Their LCM is 6. Convert: husband 3/6, consanguine sisters 4/6, uterine sisters 2/6.
3
Sum the shares and check for surplus
Add the numerators: 3+4+2 = 9. Since 9 > 6, the sums of shares exceed the estate. This triggers ‘awl.
If the sum were ≤ 6, no ‘awl would be needed.
4
Apply ‘awl by raising the denominator to the sum
Increase the denominator from 6 to 9. The new shares become: husband 3/9, consanguine sisters 4/9, uterine sisters 2/9. These fractions now sum to 1.
Alternatively, use the factor method: 100/total (149.99) ≈ 0.6667.
5
Compute final distribution in percentages or units
Use the factor: husband 50×0.6667=33.33, consanguine sisters 66.66×0.6667=44.44, uterine sisters 33.33×0.6667=22.22. Total ≈ 100.
The factor is exactly 2/3, so the final shares are 3/9, 4/9, 2/9.

Examples of 'Awl: When Shares Exceed the Base (Denominator 6 to 9 and 10)
Demonstrates two faraid cases with 'awl increasing denominator from 6 to 9 and 10.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares under 'awl when the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the base denominator.

Core Idea
'Awl reduces all shares proportionally when the sum exceeds the base denominator.

In inheritance calculations, sometimes the prescribed shares add up to more than the whole. This lesson presents two classic examples of 'awl (increase) in the Hanafi system: one where the denominator increases from 6 to 9, and another from 6 to 10. You will learn how to compute the new shares by proportionally reducing each heir's portion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their prescribed shares
List all heirs from the passage: husband, two consanguine sisters, two uterine sisters, and in the second case also mother. Note their Quranic shares: husband gets 1/2, consanguine sisters get 2/3 collectively, uterine sisters get 1/3 collectively, mother gets 1/6.
These shares are based on absence of children and absence of a male sibling for the sisters.
2
Determine the base denominator (asl al-masalah)
Find a common denominator for all shares: 1/2, 2/3, 1/3, 1/6 share denominator 6. The base is 6.
The base is the smallest number divisible by all denominators.
3
Convert shares to parts of the base and sum them
Convert each share to parts out of 6: husband = 3/6, consanguine sisters = 4/6, uterine sisters = 2/6, mother = 1/6. Sum = 3+4+2+1 = 10, which exceeds 6.
In the first example (without mother), sum is 3+4+2 = 9.
4
Apply 'awl by increasing the base denominator
Increase the base from 6 to the sum (9 or 10). The new shares are expressed with the new denominator: husband = 3/10, consanguine sisters = 4/10, uterine sisters = 2/10, mother = 1/10.
Each heir's numerator remains the same; only the denominator changes.
5
Calculate actual amounts using a set estate (e.g., 100)
Multiply each new fraction by the estate value. For the 6→10 case: husband = 3/10 × 100 = 30, consanguine sisters = 4/10 × 100 = 40, uterine sisters = 2/10 × 100 = 20, mother = 1/10 × 100 = 10. Due to rounding, the total may approximate 100.
The passage uses a calculator with factor 0.60006 to illustrate the proportional reduction.

Applying 'Awl: Husband, Sisters, and Mother
Demonstrates proportional reduction ('awl) for an inheritance exceeding 100%.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the reduced shares when the prescribed quotas exceed the estate, using the 'awl method, for the case of husband, two agnatic sisters, two uterine sisters, and mother.

Core Idea
When heirs' shares exceed the estate, 'awl reduces each share proportionally while preserving the ratios between heirs.

In this lesson, we examine a classic faraid scenario where the total of prescribed shares exceeds the estate. The Hanafi method of 'awl ensures each heir receives a proportional reduction. We will walk through the calculation step by step, using an estate of 100 dirhams as an example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heirs and Their Prescribed Shares
List all surviving heirs and their Quranic share fractions: husband (1/2), two agnatic sisters (2/3), two uterine sisters (1/3), mother (1/6).
These shares are fard (fixed portions) and come from the Quran.
2
Check if Shares Exceed the Estate
Convert the fractions to a common denominator (6) and sum them. 1/2 = 3/6, 2/3 = 4/6, 1/3 = 2/6, 1/6 = 1/6. Total = 10/6 = 1.6667, which is greater than 1.
When the sum exceeds 1, 'awl is necessary.
3
Apply the 'Awl Adjustment
Increase the denominator from 6 to the sum of numerators (10), so the new fractions become: husband 3/10, agnatic sisters 4/10, uterine sisters 2/10, mother 1/10.
Alternatively, compute a reduction factor = estate amount / total prescribed amount. Here, 100 / 166.65 ≈ 0.60006.
4
Calculate Final Shares and Verify Total
Multiply each original share amount by the reduction factor: husband 50 × 0.60006 = 30.00, agnatic sisters 66.66 × 0.60006 = 39.99, uterine sisters 33.33 × 0.60006 = 19.99, mother 16.66 × 0.60006 = 9.99. Sum = 99.97 ≈ 100.
The exact fractions yield husband 30, agnatic sisters 40, uterine sisters 20, mother 10 if no rounding.

اس مسئلے میں شوہر کو سو میں سے 50 ملا، دو باپ شریک بہنوں کو دو تہائی یعنی 66.66 ملا۔ اور دو ماں شریک بہنوں کو سو میں سے ایک تہائی یعنی 33.33 ملا۔ اور مان کو چھٹا حصہ سو میں سے 16.66 ملا۔ اور سب کا مجموعہ 166.65 ہوا ۔ چونکہ حساب سو سے ہی رکھنا ہے اس لئے 166.65 کو 100 میں تقسیم دیا تو 0.60006 کلا۔ اس کو شوہر کے حصے 50 میں ضرب دیا تو 30.00 ہوا جو شوہر کو دیا جائے گا۔ اور دو باپ شریک بہنوں کا حصہ 66.66 کو 0.60006 میں ضرب دیا تو 39.99 ہوا یہ بہن کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور ماں شریک بہن کا حصہ 33.33 کو 0.60006 میں ضرب دیا تو 19.99 آیا یہ ماں شریک بہن کا حصہ ہوگا۔ اور ماں کا حصہ 16.66 کو 0.60006 میں ضرب دیا تو 9.99 ہوا یہ ماں کو دیا جائے گا۔ ان سب کا مجموعہ 99.97 ہوا جو سو سے قریب ہے۔ اس حساب کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ سو درہم ترکہ ہو تو اس میں سے شوہر کو 30.00 دو، باپ شریک بہنوں کو 39.99 دو، ماں شریک بہنوں کو 19.99 دو۔ اور ماں کو 9.99 درہم ملے گا۔
Calculator's calculation will be as follows. Estate: 100, 'awl: 166.65, after 'awl one part is 0.60006 = 166.65 ÷ 100. Husband: 50 -> 30.00, two agnatic sisters: 66.66 -> 39.99, two uterine sisters: 33.33 -> 19.99, mother: 16.66 -> 9.99, total 99.97. The method of 'awl: In this problem, the husband received 50 out of 100, two agnatic sisters received two-thirds i.e. 66.66, two uterine sisters received one-third i.e. 33.33, mother received one-sixth i.e. 16.66, and the total is 166.65. Since the calculation is to be kept to 100, 166.65 is divided into 100 giving 0.60006. Multiply it by the husband's share 50 to get 30.00 which will be given to the husband. Multiply 66.66 by 0.60006 to get 39.99, that is the sisters' share. Multiply 33.33 by 0.60006 to get 19.99, that is the uterine sisters' share. Multiply 16.66 by 0.60006 to get 9.99, that will be given to the mother. The total of all is 99.97 which is close to 100. The meaning of this calculation is that if the estate is 100 dirhams, then give the husband 30.00, the agnatic sisters 39.99, the uterine sisters 19.99, and the mother 9.99 dirhams.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage presents a faraid (inheritance) case demonstrating the application of 'awl (proportional reduction) when the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the estate. The deceased leaves a husband, two agnatic sisters (baap shariq behnein), two uterine sisters (maan shariq behnein), and a mother. The prescribed shares are: husband 1/2, two agnatic sisters 2/3, two uterine sisters 1/3, mother 1/6. These fractions do not sum to 1; they sum to 1.6667 (166.67%). Therefore, the estate of 100 dirhams is insufficient to pay the full shares. The 'awl method proportionally reduces each share. The calculation is done by setting the shares relative to 100 (husband 50, agnatic sisters 66.66, uterine sisters 33.33, mother 16.66, total 166.65) and then finding the reduction factor (100/166.65 = 0.60006). Multiplying each original share by this factor yields the reduced amounts (husband 30.00, agnatic sisters 39.99, uterine sisters 19.99, mother 9.99). The total after reduction becomes 99.97, effectively 100. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of 'awl: decrease each share proportionally so the total equals the estate.

Key Terms
عول (ʻawl): Proportional reduction of shares when the prescribed heirs' shares exceed the total estate.
باپ شریک بہن (baap shariq behn): Agnatic sister (full sister or sister sharing the same father).
ماں شریک بہن (maan shariq behn): Uterine sister (sister sharing the same mother only).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the given inheritance case, what is the final share of the husband after 'awl on an estate of 100 dirhams?
A) 50 dirhams
B) 30 dirhams
C) 40 dirhams
D) 25 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each heir's share so that the total equals the estate, preserving the relative ratios between heirs.

Calculating 'Awl When a Quarter Combines with a Third or Sixth: The Case of 'Awl to 13
States the rule for 'awl when quarter with third or sixth, and illustrates 'awl to 13.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when heirs entitled to 1/4, 2/3, and 1/6 combine, applying 'awl to a new base of 13.

Core Idea
When wife (1/4), two+ sisters (2/3), and mother (1/6) inherit, base 12 'awls to 13.

Inheritance calculations sometimes exceed the whole estate, requiring 'awl (increase of the base denominator). The Hanafi school uses a systematic method: start with the least common multiple (asl al-masalah) of the share denominators, then adjust upward when total numerators exceed it. This lesson takes you through the classic case where a quarter (1/4) meets a third (2/3) and a sixth (1/6) — the base of 12 must 'awl to 13. We'll work step by step from the rule to the final shares, including a practical example with numbers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the combination
Recognise that the phrase 'quarter with a third or sixth' means a spouse (1/4) exists alongside siblings (2/3) or a parent (1/6). The passage tells us the base is always 12.
Remember: Asl al-masalah for 1/4, 1/3, 1/6 is 12 because LCM of 4,3,6 = 12.
2
Convert shares to the common base
Write each Quranic share as a fraction of 12: wife = 1/4 = 3/12; two full sisters = 2/3 = 8/12; mother = 1/6 = 2/12.
3
Sum the numerators
Add the converted shares: 3 + 8 + 2 = 13. Since this exceeds the base of 12, 'awl is required.
4
Apply 'awl: increase the denominator to the sum
The new base becomes the sum of the numerators (13). Each heir's share is now their original numerator over the new denominator: wife 3/13, sisters 8/13, mother 2/13.
This is the Hanafi method: asl al-masalah becomes the total of numerators after 'awl.
5
Convert to an estate amount (optional)
To find actual monetary shares, multiply each fraction by the estate value. For an estate of 100, wife gets 100 × 3/13 ≈ 23.08, sisters 61.54, mother 15.38. The passage gives approximate values 23.07, 61.53, 15.37 due to rounding.
The calculator method in the text uses a reduction factor (100/108.32 ≈ 0.9231) applied to original percentage shares, which yields the same result.

Source Text

۳۲۵۸] (۶) اگر چوتھائی کے ساتھ تہائی ہو یا چھٹا ہو تو اصل مسئلہ بارہ سے ہوگا اور عول کرے گا تیرہ ، پندرہ اور سترہ کی طرف۔ تشرح اگر چوتھائی کے ساتھ تہائی لینے والا ہو، یا چھٹا لینے والا ہوتو مسئلہ بارہ سے چلے گا۔ لیکن کبھی ایسے بھی لینے والے ہوں گے کہ ان کا حصہ زیادہ ہو کر بارہ کے بجائے تیرہ ہو جائے گا، کبھی پندرہ ہو جائے گا اور کبھی سترہ ہو جائے گا۔ تفصیل نیچے دیکھیں۔ تیرہ کی طرف عول کی صورت یہ ہے : میت نے بیوی اور دو حقیقی بہنیں اور ماں چھوڑی تو بیوی کو چوتھائی ، دو حقیقی بہنوں کو دو تہائی اور ماں کو چھٹا ملے گا، مسئلہ بارہ سے چلے گا۔ لیکن تمام حصے مل کر تیرہ حصے ہو جائیں گے جس کو عول کہتے ہیں۔ مسئلہ اس طرح ہوگا۔ میت 12 عول 13 بیوی 3 دو حقیقی بہنیں 8 ماں 2 کلکیولیٹر کا حساب اس طرح ہوگا۔ میت 100 عول 108.32 عول کے بعد ایک حصہ 0.9231 = 108.32 : 100 بیوی 25 23.07 دو حقیقی بہنیں 66.66 61.53 ماں 16.66 15.37 عول کا طریقہ اس مسئلے میں بیوی کو چوتھائی میں سے 25 دیا۔ اور دو حقیقی بہنوں کو دو تہائی یعنی سو میں سے 66.66 دیا۔ اور ماں کو چھٹا حصہ یعنی 16.66 دیا۔ سب کا مجموعہ 108.32 ہوا جو سو سے زیادہ ہے اور عول ہے۔ اب چونکہ حساب سو سے ہی رکھنا ہے اس لئے 108.32 کو 100 میں تقسیم دیا تو 0.9231 آیا۔ جو ایک حصہ ہے اس کو بیوی کے 25 میں ضرب دیا تو 23.07 ہوا جو بیوی کا حصہ عول کے بعد ہوا۔ اور 66.66 کو 0.9231 میں ضرب دیا تو 61.53 ہوا جو دونوں بہنوں کا حصہ ہوانے اور ماں کا حصہ 16.66 کو 0.9231 میں ضرب دیا تو 15.37 ہوا۔ اور سب کا مجموعہ 99.97 ہوا جو سو کے قریب ہے۔ دو پیسے کا حساب کلکو لیٹر نے نہیں دیا ہے۔
And if with the quarter there is a third or a sixth, its base is from twelve and it 'awls to thirteen, fifteen, and seventeen. [Commentary:] If there is a third or a sixth along with the quarter, the base is twelve. But sometimes the shares become more than twelve, becoming thirteen, sometimes fifteen, and sometimes seventeen. See details below. The case of 'awl to thirteen: The deceased left a wife, two full sisters, and a mother. The wife gets one-fourth, the two full sisters two-thirds, and the mother one-sixth. The base is twelve, but the total shares become thirteen, which is called 'awl. The problem becomes: deceased 12, 'awl 13, wife 3, two full sisters 8, mother 2. Method of 'awl: In this problem, the wife received from the quarter 25, the two full sisters two-thirds i.e. 66.66, and the mother one-sixth i.e. 16.66. Total is 108.32 which exceeds 100, so 'awl applies. Since the calculation is to be kept at 100, 108.32 is divided into 100 giving 0.9231. Multiply the wife's share 25 by 0.9231 to get 23.07, the sisters' share 66.66 to get 61.53, the mother's share 16.66 to get 15.37. Total is 99.97, close to 100. Commentary
This passage first states the core ruling: when an inheritance includes an heir entitled to a quarter (e.g., wife) along with an heir entitled to a third (e.g., two or more full sisters) or a sixth (e.g., mother), the base denominator (asl al-masalah) is 12. However, the shares may add up to more than 12, requiring 'awl. The 'awl can increase the base to 13, 15, or 17 depending on the specific heirs. Then the commentator explains the case of 'awl to 13: the heirs are a wife (1/4 = 3/12), two full sisters (2/3 = 8/12), and a mother (1/6 = 2/12). The total is 13/12, so the denominator increases to 13. The shares become: wife 3/13, two full sisters 8/13, mother 2/13. The text then shows a calculator method using 100 as base: original shares out of 100: wife 25, sisters 66.66, mother 16.66, total 108.32. The reduction factor 100/108.32 ≈ 0.9231 is applied to get final shares: wife 23.07, sisters 61.53, mother 15.37 (totalling approximately 100). This is the same as the fraction method: 3/13 of 100 ≈ 23.08, 8/13 ≈ 61.54, 2/13 ≈ 15.38. The small rounding difference is noted.

Key Terms
عول (ʻawl): Increase in the denominator of the inheritance base when shares exceed the whole.
اصل مسئلہ (asl al-masalah): The least common multiple of the share denominators used as the base for inheritance calculations.
چوتھائی (chothaai): One-fourth (1/4), the share of a spouse when the deceased has no child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a quarter is combined with a third or sixth, the base starts at 12 and 'awls to the sum of numerators (13, 15, or 17); in the example, it goes to 13.

Calculating 'Awl to 15: Wife, Full Sisters, and Consanguine Sisters
Illustrates 'awl to 15 with quarter and two-thirds and one-third shares.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares when a wife, two full sisters, and two consanguine sisters survive, applying 'awl to 15.

Core Idea
When shares exceed the estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each share—here from 12 to 15.

This lesson walks through a classic Hanafi faraid scenario: a wife inheriting 1/4, two full sisters 2/3, and two consanguine sisters 1/3. The total exceeds the whole, so 'awl is applied, converting the base from 12 to 15. We'll see both the fractional and decimal calculation methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify heirs and their Quranic shares
List all heirs: wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), two consanguine sisters (1/3). Note that consanguine sisters are not excluded when there are only two full sisters.
Consanguine sisters inherit 1/3 when there are no children and full sisters exist.
2
Find the base denominator (asl al-masalah)
Convert shares to a common denominator: 1/4, 2/3, 1/3 LCM = 12. So wife = 3/12, full sisters = 8/12, consanguine sisters = 4/12.
Total = 15/12, which exceeds 1.
3
Apply 'awl to adjust the denominator
Since total shares (15/12) exceed the whole (1), increase the denominator to the total numerator: new denominator = 15. Shares become wife 3/15, full sisters 8/15, consanguine sisters 4/15.
This is 'awl to 15.
4
Calculate final shares for a given estate value
For an estate of 100, multiply each fraction by 100: wife = 20, full sisters ≈ 53.33, consanguine sisters ≈ 26.67.
Calculator method verifies: original shares sum to 124.99, reduction factor = 100/124.99 ≈ 0.80006.
5
Verify total sums to estate value
20 + 53.33 + 26.67 = 100.00. Slight rounding differences are acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پندرہ تک عول کی صورت یہ ہے : میت نے بیوی، دو حقیقی بہنیں اور دو ماں شریک بہنیں چھوڑی۔ اس لئے بیوی کو چوتھائی ، دو حقیقی بہنوں کو دو تہائی اور دو ماں شریک بہنوں کو ایک تہائی دی جائے گی۔ اس لئے مسئلہ بارہ سے چلے گا اور حصے پندرہ ہو جائیں گے۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔ میت 12 عول 15 بیوی 3 دو حقیقی بہنیں 8 دوماں شریک بہنیں 4 کلکولیٹر کا حساب اس طرح ہوگا ۔ میت 100 عول 124.99 عول کے بعد ایک حصہ 0.80006 = 124.99 × 100 بیوی 25 20.00 دو حقیقی بہنیں 66.66 53.33 دو ماں شریک بہنیں 33.33 26.66
The case of 'awl to fifteen: The deceased left a wife, two full sisters, and two consanguine sisters. Therefore, the wife gets one-fourth, the two full sisters two-thirds, and the two consanguine sisters one-third. So the base is twelve, and the shares become fifteen. The problem becomes: deceased 12, 'awl 15, wife 3, two full sisters 8, two consanguine sisters 4. Calculator calculation: estate 100, 'awl 124.99, after 'awl one part = 0.80006 = 100/124.99. Wife: 25 -> 20.00, two full sisters: 66.66 -> 53.33, two consanguine sisters: 33.33 -> 26.66.

Commentary
This passage gives the second example of 'awl when a quarter is present along with a third or sixth. Here the heirs are: wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), and two consanguine sisters (1/3). The base is 12: wife 3/12, full sisters 8/12, consanguine sisters 4/12, total 15/12. Hence 'awl to 15. The final shares: wife 3/15 = 1/5, full sisters 8/15, consanguine sisters 4/15. The text then shows a calculator method using 100 as base: original shares out of 100: wife 25, full sisters 66.66, consanguine sisters 33.33, total 124.99. Reduction factor = 100/124.99 ≈ 0.80006. Final shares: wife 20.00, full sisters 53.33, consanguine sisters 26.66. This matches the fractional method: 3/15 of 100 = 20, 8/15 ≈ 53.33, 4/15 ≈ 26.67 (rounding difference).

Key Terms
حقیقی بہن (haqiqi behn): Full sister (same father and mother).
ماں شریک بہن (maan shariq behn): Consanguine sister (same father, different mother).
عول (ʻawl): Proportional increase of the base denominator when shares exceed the whole.

Key Takeaway
When a wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), and two consanguine sisters (1/3) inherit, the base 'awls from 12 to 15, giving the wife 3/15, full sisters 8/15, and consanguine sisters 4/15 of the estate.

Awl Case: Wife, Two Full Sisters, Mother
Explains 'awl calculation for wife, two full sisters, mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares for a wife, two full sisters, and mother when 'awl applies, using both the traditional fraction method (base 12) and the percentage method (base 100).

Core Idea
When shares exceed the estate, 'awl reduces each share proportionally, preserving the relative ratios.

This lesson examines a classic faraid case involving a wife, two full sisters, and a mother. The prescribed shares total 13/12 of the estate, requiring 'awl (proportional reduction). We will walk through two calculation methods: the traditional fractional approach and a percentage-based method. Understanding both reinforces the principle that 'awl adjusts the base without altering the heirs' relative entitlements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heirs and Their Prescribed Shares
List the wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), mother (1/6). Note the conditions for each share: wife gets 1/4 if no child, sisters get 2/3 if no father/grandfather and more than one, mother gets 1/6 if deceased has siblings.
Shares are fixed by Quranic text.
2
Determine the Base Number (Asl al-Mas'alah)
Find the LCM of denominators 4, 3, 6 = 12. Convert shares: wife 3/12, sisters 8/12, mother 2/12.
The base represents the denominator of the common fraction.
3
Check for 'Awl
Sum the numerators: 3+8+2 = 13, which exceeds the base 12. Thus 'awl applies: increase the base to 13. Final shares: wife 3/13, sisters 8/13, mother 2/13.
Each share is reduced proportionally; the fractions are preserved.
4
Apply the Percentage Method
Set estate = 100 units. Assign percentages: wife 25%, sisters 66.66%, mother 16.66%. Total 108.32%. Compute 'awl factor = 100/108.32 ≈ 0.9231. Multiply: wife 23.07, sisters 61.53, mother 15.37.
This method provides concrete numbers for distribution.
5
Compare Both Methods
The fraction method gives exact fractions (wife 3/13 ≈ 23.0769%), the percentage method rounds to 23.07%. Both are valid; the fraction method is exact for divisible estates.
Understanding both methods reinforces the concept of proportional reduction.

عول کا طریقہ
اس مسئلے میں بیوی کو چوتھائی میں سے 25 دیا۔ اور دو حقیقی بہنوں کو دو تہائی یعنی سو میں سے 66.66 دیا۔ اور ماں کو چھٹا حصہ یعنی 16.66 دیا۔ سب کا مجموعہ 108.32 ہوا جو سو سے زیادہ ہے اور عول ہے۔ اب چونکہ حساب سو سے ہی رکھنا ہے اس لئے 108.32 کو 100 میں تقسیم دیا تو 0.9231 آیا۔ جو ایک حصہ ہے اس کو بیوی کے 25 میں ضرب دیا تو 23.07 ہوا جو بیوی کا حصہ عول کے بعد ہوا۔ اور 66.66 کو 0.9231 میں ضرب دیا تو 61.53 ہوا جو دونوں بہنوں کا حصہ ہوانے اور ماں کا حصہ 16.66 کو 0.9231 میں ضرب دیا تو 15.37 ہوا۔ اور سب کا مجموعہ 99.97 ہوا جو سو کے قریب ہے۔ دو پیسے کا حساب کلکو لیٹر نے نہیں دیا ہے۔
The case will be like this. Deceased: base 12, 'awl 13. Wife: 3. Two full sisters: 8. Mother: 2. The calculator's calculation will be like this: Deceased: 100, 'awl 108.32, after 'awl one share = 0.9231 = 100 / 108.32. Wife: 25 → 23.07. Two full sisters: 66.66 → 61.53. Mother: 16.66 → 15.37. Section on Calculation of Inheritances. After 'awl: mother gets [calculated]; after 'awl: full sisters get; after 'awl: wife gets; total: 16.66 × 0.9231 = 15.37; 66.66 × 0.9231 = 61.53; 25 × 0.9231 = 23.07; sum = 99.97. Method of 'awl: In this case, wife is given 25 (1/4 of 100), two full sisters are given two-thirds (66.66 of 100), mother is given one-sixth (16.66). Their total is 108.32, which exceeds 100, so 'awl applies. Since the calculation is kept at 100, 108.32 is divided into 100, giving 0.9231 per share. Multiply by wife's 25 gives 23.07, her share after 'awl. Multiply 66.66 by 0.9231 gives 61.53, the sisters' share. Multiply mother's share 16.66 by 0.9231 gives 15.37. Total is 99.97, near 100. The calculator did not give the two paisa fraction.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a faraid (inheritance) case demonstrating 'awl (proportional reduction) when prescribed shares exceed the estate. The heirs are: wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), mother (1/6). The base is 12 (LCM of denominators 4,3,6): wife 3/12, sisters 8/12, mother 2/12. Total 13/12, so 'awl increases the base to 13. The author then explains using a percentage method: taking the estate as 100 for calculation. Wife gets 25% (1/4), sisters 66.66% (2/3), mother 16.66% (1/6). Total exceeds 100%, so 'awl reduces each share proportionally by dividing 100 by total (108.32) giving factor ~0.9231. Multiplying each share gives final percentages: wife 23.07%, sisters 61.53%, mother 15.37%, summing to ~100%. This illustrates the Hanafi method of 'awl where shares are reduced ratably.

Key Terms
عول (awl): Increase in the base number of the inheritance to accommodate shares exceeding the estate.

Key Takeaway
When shares exceed the estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each share by increasing the base number, preserving the relative ratios prescribed by the Quran.

'Awl with Wife, Full Sisters, and Consanguine Sisters
Explains 'awl calculation for wife, two full sisters, two consanguine sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distributed shares when 'awl occurs with wife, two full sisters, and two consanguine sisters using the Hanafi method.

Core Idea
When shares exceed the base, 'awl scales them proportionally without altering Quranic ratios.

This passage demonstrates the 'awl mechanism in Hanafi faraid. When a wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), and two consanguine sisters (1/3) inherit together, the total exceeds the base 12, requiring 'awl to increase the base to 15. Understanding this calculation is essential for correctly distributing an estate when shares overshoot.

Guided Path
1
Identify heirs and prescribed shares
List all heirs: wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), two consanguine sisters (1/3). These are the Quranic fixed shares (fard).
All three prescribed shares are fard; no asabah present.
2
Determine asl al-masalah (base number)
Find the LCM of the denominators 4, 3, 3. The LCM is 12. This is the base before 'awl.
Alternatively, use the smallest common multiple that allows whole parts for each share.
3
Assign shares as parts of the base
Convert each prescribed share into parts of base 12: wife 1/4 = 3/12, full sisters 2/3 = 8/12, consanguine sisters 1/3 = 4/12.
For multiple heirs of the same category, the part is for the group; later each individual gets half if they are two.
4
Check for 'awl (excess over base)
Add the parts: 3 + 8 + 4 = 15. Since 15 > 12, 'awl applies. The base is increased to 15.
'awl does not change the relative proportions; it only increases the denominator.
5
Calculate final shares as fractions of new base
After 'awl, the new shares are: wife 3/15, full sisters 8/15, consanguine sisters 4/15. Each individual full sister gets 4/15, each consanguine sister gets 2/15.
The calculator method shown in the passage uses percentages for illustration but the underlying fractions are the same.

The form of 'awl up to fifteen is: The deceased left a wife, two full sisters, and two consanguine sisters. So the wife gets one-fourth, the two full sisters get two-thirds, and the two consanguine sisters get one-third. Therefore the case proceeds from twelve and the shares become fifteen. The case will be as follows: Deceased: base 12, 'awl 15. Wife: 3. Two full sisters: 8. Two consanguine sisters: 4. The calculator's calculation will be like this: Deceased: 100, 'awl 124.99, after 'awl one share = 0.80006 = 100 / 124.99. Wife: 25 → 20.00. Two full sisters: 66.66 → 53.33. Two consanguine sisters: 33.33 → 26.66. After 'awl: consanguine sisters get; after 'awl: full sisters get; after 'awl: wife gets; total: 33.33 × 0.80006 = 26.66; 66.66 × 0.80006 = 53.33; 25 × 0.80006 = 20.00; sum = 99.99. Section on Calculation of Inheritances. Method of 'awl: In this case, wife is given 25 (1/4 of 100), two full sisters are given two-thirds (66.66), and two consanguine sisters are given one-third (33.33). Their total is 124.99. So 100 is divided by it, giving 0.80006. Then multiply 25 by 0.80006 gives 20.00, the wife's share. Multiply 66.66 by 0.80006 gives 53.33, the two full sisters' share. Multiply 33.33 by 0.80006 gives 26.66, the two consanguine sisters' share. Total is 99.99, near 100. The meaning of this calculation: if the deceased left 100 dirhams, the wife gets 20.00, the full sisters 53.33, the consanguine sisters 26.66. One sister of the pair gets half: 13.33.

Commentary
This passage is a faraid case demonstrating 'awl with four heirs: wife (1/4), two full sisters (2/3), and two consanguine sisters (1/3). Note that consanguine sisters get one-third when there are two or more (as per Hanafi rulings), but here they are combined with full sisters. However, the shares given (2/3 and 1/3) actually sum to 1, but with wife's 1/4, total exceeds 1. The base is 12: wife 3, full sisters 8, consanguine sisters 4 (since 1/3 of 12 is 4). Sum is 15, so 'awl increases base to 15. Final shares: wife 3/15 = 1/5, full sisters 8/15, consanguine sisters 4/15. The calculator method uses 100 as estate: wife 25%, full sisters 66.66%, consanguine sisters 33.33%, total 124.99%, factor 0.80006. After 'awl: wife 20%, full sisters 53.33%, consanguine sisters 26.66%. Note that each consanguine sister gets half of 26.66 = 13.33, as mentioned.

Key Terms
ماں شریک بہن (maan shariq behn): Consanguine sister (same father, different mother).
عول ('awl): An adjustment where the base number (asl al-masalah) is increased because the total prescribed shares exceed the whole estate.
اصل المسئلہ (asl al-masalah): The base number (denominator) from which shares are derived, usually the LCM of the share denominators.

Key Takeaway
When prescribed shares exceed the base, 'awl proportionally increases the base (denominator) so that all heirs receive their correct relative shares.

Calculating 'Awl with Wife, Sisters, and Mother
Explaining 'awl calculation for a specific inheritance case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares for a case involving wife, full sisters, consanguine sisters, and mother, applying the principle of 'awl (proportional reduction) correctly.

Core Idea
'Awl proportionally reduces all shares when the sum of prescribed fractions exceeds the entire estate.

This lesson works through a specific inheritance case where the Quranic shares sum to more than the estate. You will learn how to identify the prescribed shares, find the base number, and apply 'awl to reduce each share proportionally. The case involves a wife, two full sisters, two consanguine sisters, and a mother.

Guided Path
1
List the Heirs and Their Quranic Shares
Identify each heir and their prescribed fraction from the Quran. Wife gets 1/4 (no children), two full sisters get 2/3, two consanguine sisters get 1/3, mother gets 1/6.
Shares are fixed; check conditions like absence of children or male siblings.
2
Find the Base Number (Asl al-Mas'alah)
Calculate the least common multiple (LCM) of the denominators (4, 3, 3, 6) which is 12. Convert each share to twelfths: wife 3/12, full sisters 8/12, consanguine sisters 4/12, mother 2/12.
The LCM ensures all shares are expressed with a common denominator.
3
Check if 'Awl is Needed
Add the numerators: 3 + 8 + 4 + 2 = 17. Since 17 > 12, the total exceeds the estate, so 'awl is required.
'Awl increases the base number to the sum of numerators.
4
Apply 'Awl
Set the new base to 17. Each share becomes a fraction with denominator 17: wife 3/17, full sisters 8/17, consanguine sisters 4/17, mother 2/17.
The estate is now divided into 17 equal parts instead of 12.
5
Calculate Final Shares from Estate
If the estate is 100 dirhams, multiply each fraction by 100: wife 100 × 3/17 ≈ 17.65, full sisters 100 × 8/17 ≈ 47.06, consanguine sisters 100 × 4/17 ≈ 23.53, mother 100 × 2/17 ≈ 11.76.
The total is approximately 100 due to rounding.

Commentary
This is a faraid case demonstrating the method of 'awl (proportional reduction) when the total of prescribed shares exceeds the estate. This illustrates the principle of 'awl: when shares exceed the estate, each share is reduced proportionally.

Calculating 'awl with Eighth and Two Sixths
Explaining 'awl calculation when eighth and two sixths are present

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares using 'awl when the estate includes a wife, two daughters, father, and mother, and state the final shares after proportional reduction.

Core Idea
When prescribed shares exceed the estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each share.

In Hanafi inheritance law, when a deceased leaves a wife, two daughters, father, and mother, the prescribed shares sum to more than the whole estate. This lesson walks through the method of 'awl (proportional reduction) using the base number 24. You will learn how to adjust the shares so that the estate is divided fairly according to Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heirs and Their Prescribed Shares
List all heirs: wife (1/8 when children exist), two daughters (2/3 when no son), father (1/6), mother (1/6). Write each share as a fraction of the estate.
Check the conditions for each share: wife gets 1/8 because of the daughters; father and mother each get 1/6 because of children.
2
Find the Base Number (Asl al-Mas'alah)
Determine the common denominator (LCM) of the denominators: 8, 3, 6, 6. The LCM is 24. Convert each share to units of 24: wife = 3/24, daughters = 16/24, father = 4/24, mother = 4/24.
The base number is the starting point for calculating shares.
3
Sum the Shares and Detect 'Awl
Add the numerators: 3+16+4+4 = 27. The total is 27/24, which is greater than 1. Since the estate is only 1 (the whole), the shares must be reduced. This situation is called 'awl.
'Awl occurs when the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the estate.
4
Apply 'Awl: Increase the Base to the Total
The new base becomes the total numerator, 27. Each heir's share is now expressed out of 27. Wife = 3/27, daughters = 16/27, father = 4/27, mother = 4/27.
All shares are reduced proportionally. This is the standard Hanafi method.
5
Calculate Actual Shares Using an Example Estate
Assume the estate is 100 dirhams. Multiply each fraction by 100. Wife: 100 × 3/27 ≈ 11.11, daughters: 100 × 16/27 ≈ 59.26, father: 100 × 4/27 ≈ 14.81, mother: 100 × 4/27 ≈ 14.81. Total = 99.99 ≈ 100.
The text also shows a reduction factor method (100/112.48) which yields the same result.

[3259] (7) If with the eighth there are two sixths or two thirds, then the base of the case is from twenty-four and it will undergo 'awl to twenty-seven. When there is one who takes an eighth and two persons each taking a sixth, the case proceeds from twenty-four and will undergo 'awl to twenty-seven. The case of 'awl to twenty-seven is as follows: The deceased left a wife, two daughters, and a father and mother. Since there are children, the wife gets one-eighth. The two daughters get two-thirds, the father gets one-sixth, and the mother gets one-sixth. Therefore, the case proceeds from twenty-four. The total of all shares will become twenty-seven, which is called 'awl. The case proceeds as follows: Deceased 24, 'awl 27; Wife: 3; Two daughters: 16; Father: 4; Mother: 4. The calculator calculation is as follows: Deceased 100, 'awl 112.48; after 'awl, one share is 0.8890 (ratio 100:112.48). Wife: 12.5, after 'awl 11.11; Two daughters: 66.66, after 'awl 59.26; Father: 16.66, after 'awl 14.81; Mother: 16.66, after 'awl 14.81; Total: 99.99. After 'awl, mother gets 14.81; after 'awl, father gets 14.81; after 'awl, daughters get 59.26; after 'awl, wife gets 11.11. Total... Method of 'awl: In this case, the wife was given one-eighth, i.e., 12.5 out of 100. The girls were given two-thirds, i.e., 66.66 out of 100. The father was given one-sixth, i.e., 16.66 out of 100. And the mother was also given one-sixth, i.e., 16.66 out of 100. The sum of all is 112.48. Divide 100 by this, you get 0.8890, which will be one share. Multiply the wife's share 12.5 by 0.8890, you get 11.11, which is the wife's share. And 66.66 by...

Commentary
This is a faraid case illustrating 'awl when the estate includes a wife (1/8), two daughters (2/3), father (1/6), and mother (1/6). The prescribed shares: wife 1/8 = 3/24, two daughters 2/3 = 16/24, father 1/6 = 4/24, mother 1/6 = 4/24; total = 27/24, exceeding 1. Thus the base 24 undergoes 'awl to 27. The author shows the calculation method using an estate of 100 units. The total shares sum to 112.48 (representing 27/24 of 100). The reduction factor is 100/112.48 ≈ 0.8890. Applying this factor: wife gets 12.5 × 0.8890 = 11.11, daughters 66.66 × 0.8890 = 59.26, father 16.66 × 0.8890 = 14.81, mother similarly 14.81. The total after reduction is 99.99, approximating 100. This demonstrates the rule that when the estate includes an eighth and two sixths, the base is 24 and 'awl goes to 27.

Key Terms
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of shares when total prescribed shares exceed the estate; the base number increases to the total.
ثمن (thumn): One-eighth share, prescribed for a wife when there are children.
أصل المسألة (asl al-mas'alah): The base number from which shares are calculated; the least common multiple of the denominators of the shares.

Key Takeaway
When the prescribed shares exceed the entire estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each share by increasing the base number to the total numerator.

Calculating 'Awl with 1/8, 1/6, and 2/3: Base 24 to 27
Explaining base number 24 and 'awl to 27 for specific fractions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares for a deceased leaving a wife, two daughters, father, and mother, using 'awl to adjust the base from 24 to 27.

Core Idea
When fixed shares exceed the estate, 'awl proportionally reduces each share without excluding any heir.

In this lesson, we examine a classic faraid scenario where the fixed shares (1/8 for wife, 2/3 for two daughters, and 1/6 each for father and mother) add up to more than the whole estate. The Hanafi school applies 'awl (proportional increase of the base denominator) to ensure all heirs receive a reduced but fair share. This example walks you through the calculation from base 24 to 'awl to 27, using both fractional and decimal methods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their fixed shares
List all Quranic heirs: wife (1/8), two daughters (2/3), father (1/6), mother (1/6). Note that each share is a fixed fraction of the estate.
The shares are prescribed by the Quran; no asabah (residuary) here because all shares are fixed.
2
Determine the base number (asl al-mas'alah)
Find the least common multiple (LCM) of the denominators of all shares: 8, 3, and 6. LCM = 24. This is the base denominator.
LCM ensures all shares are expressed as whole numbers: 1/8 = 3/24, 2/3 = 16/24, 1/6 = 4/24 each.
3
Sum the shares and compare to the base
Add the numerators: 3 (wife) + 16 (daughters) + 4 (father) + 4 (mother) = 27. This sum exceeds the base (27 > 24), so the estate cannot cover all shares at face value.
When the sum exceeds the base, 'awl (increase of the base) becomes necessary.
4
Apply 'awl by increasing the base to the sum
Increase the base number from 24 to 27. Each share's numerator remains the same, but the denominator becomes 27. Thus, wife gets 3/27, daughters 16/27, father 4/27, mother 4/27.
The shares are now proportional fractions of the estate that sum to 27/27 = 1.
5
Calculate individual shares from the estate value
If the estate is 100 dirhams, multiply by each fraction: wife: 100 * (3/27) ≈ 11.11; daughters: 100 * (16/27) ≈ 59.26; father: 100 * (4/27) ≈ 14.81; mother: 100 * (4/27) ≈ 14.81. Total ≈ 99.99 (rounding).
The calculation can also be done by finding one share value (100/27 ≈ 3.7037) and multiplying by each share's number.

(7) If with the eighth there are two sixth shares or two thirds, then the base of the problem is from twenty-four and it will 'awl to twenty-seven. When in the problem there is a taker of an eighth and two persons taking a sixth each, the problem proceeds from four and will 'awl to twenty-seven. The manner of 'awl to twenty-seven is: The deceased left a wife, two daughters, and a mother and father. There is offspring, so the wife gets an eighth share. The two daughters get two-thirds, the father gets a sixth, and the mother gets a sixth. So the problem proceeds from four. The shares together become twenty-seven, which is called 'awl. The problem proceeds thus: the deceased [base] 24, 'awl to 27: wife 3, two daughters 16, mother 4, father 4. The calculator's calculation is as follows: main 100, 'awl amount 112.48, after 'awl one share is 0.8890 = 1:12.48 : 100. Wife 16.66, two daughters 66.66, father 16.66, mother 16.66.
