The method of 'awl: In this problem, the wife was given an eighth, i.e., 12.5 out of 100. The girls were given two-thirds, i.e., 66.66 out of 100. The father was given a sixth, i.e., 16.66 out of 100. The mother was also given a sixth share, i.e., 16.66 out of 100. The total of all is 112.48. Divide 100 by this, yielding 0.8890, which is one share. Multiply the wife's share 12.5 by 0.8890, giving 11.11, which is the wife's share. Multiply 66.66 by 0.8890, giving 59.26, which is the two daughters' share. Multiply 16.66 by 0.8890, giving 14.81, which is the father's share. Multiply the mother's share 16.66 by 0.8890, giving 14.81, which is the mother's share. The total of all is 99.99, approximately 100. Actually, the calculator gives one part per thousand of a new paisa, but for convenience the remainder is dropped. The meaning of this calculation is that if the deceased left 100 dirhams, then the wife gets 11.11, the two daughters 59.26, the father 14.81, and the mother 14.81 dirhams.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an example on 'awl (proportional increase of the base) in inheritance. The author states that when the estate includes a 1/8 share together with either two 1/6 shares or 2/3 shares, the base number (asl al-mas'alah) is 24, but the total shares exceed the base (adding up to 27/24), so the base is increased ('awl) to 27. The Urdu commentary provides a concrete example: a deceased leaves a wife, two daughters, father, and mother. The wife gets 1/8 (3/24), the two daughters get 2/3 (16/24 collectively), the father gets 1/6 (4/24), and the mother gets 1/6 (4/24). The sum is 27/24, so 'awl is applied: the new base becomes 27, and each share is proportionally reduced. The commentary then demonstrates the same calculation using 100 dirhams as the estate, showing the reduction to percentages. The teacher should emphasize that 'awl is necessary when the Quranic shares exceed the estate, and that the base of 24 is chosen as the LCM of the denominator 8, 3, and 6.

Key Terms
عول (‘awl): Increase in the base number (asl al-mas'alah) when the sum of fixed shares exceeds the estate
ثمن (thumn): The fixed share of one-eighth, given to a spouse when the deceased has a child
سدس (suds): The fixed share of one-sixth, given to parents or siblings under certain conditions

Tashih: Correcting the Base When Shares Don't Divide Evenly
Explaining method to adjust base when a group's shares do not divide evenly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tashih to correct the inheritance base when a group of heirs receives shares that do not divide evenly among them.

Core Idea
If a group's shares do not divide evenly, multiply the group size by the base to get integer shares.

In inheritance calculations, we often assign shares as fractions of a base number. When a group of multiple heirs (e.g., two brothers) collectively receives a number of shares that does not divide evenly among them, we need to adjust the base so that each heir gets a whole number of shares. This process is called tashih (correction). The rule is straightforward: multiply the number of heirs in that group by the original base. The resulting new base is divisible by all shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their categories
List every surviving heir and determine whether they are Quranic fixed-share heirs (fard) or residuary heirs (asabah). For each fard heir, note the fraction. For asabah, note that they receive the residue.
In this lesson's example: wife (fard, 1/4) and two full brothers (asabah).
2
Set the initial base (asl al-masalah)
Choose the smallest number that allows all fard fractions to be expressed as integers. Usually this is the least common multiple of the denominators.
Base = 4 (denominator of 1/4). Wife takes 1 share; residue 3 shares for brothers.
3
Check divisibility for each group
For every group of multiple heirs sharing the same category (e.g., two brothers, three sons), see whether the total number of shares assigned to that group divides evenly by the number of individuals in that group.
Brothers have 3 shares for 2 persons → 3 ÷ 2 = 1.5, not integer.
4
Apply tashih if needed
If a group's shares do not divide evenly, multiply the original base (and all shares) by the number of individuals in that group. This gives a new base and new integer share numbers for every heir.
Multiply base 4 by 2 (number of brothers) → new base = 8. Wife's shares become 1×2=2, brothers' shares become 3×2=6, each brother gets 3.
5
Verify the result
After tashih, confirm that every heir receives a whole number of shares and that the sum of all shares equals the new base.
2+6=8, correct. Each brother gets 6/2=3, integer.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا انقسمت المسئلة على الورثة فقد صحت وان لم تنقسم سهام فريق منهم عليهم فاضرب عددهم في اصل المسئلة وعولها ان كانت عائلة. (۸) جب مسئلہ تقسیم ہو جائے ورثہ پر تو صحیح ہے۔ اور اگر تقسیم نہ ہو ان میں سے کسی فریق کا حصہ لینے والے پر تو اس کے عدد کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دو۔ اور اس کے عول کو اگر عول والا ہو۔ پس جو حاصل ضرب ہو اس سے مسئلہ صحیح ہوگا۔ جیسے بیوی اور دو بھائی۔ پس بیوی کے لئے چوتھائی ہے ایک حصہ اور دو بھائیوں کے لئے بقیہ تین حصے ہیں جو ان پر تقسیم نہیں ہوتے۔ پس دو کو ضرب دیں اصل مسئلہ میں تو یہ آٹھ ہو جائیں گے۔ اور اسی سے مسئلہ صحیح ہوگا۔ جتنا حصہ فریق کو ملاوہ اس کے عدد پر تقسیم ہو جاتا ہو تب تو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ مثلا دوسہام ملے تھے اور لینے والے دو بھائی تھے تو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ لیکن اگر تین سہام ملے اور لینے والے دو بھائی ہیں تو دو کو تین سہام ڈیڑھ ڈیڑھ ہو گا جو کسر ہے۔ اس لئے دو بھائی کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دے کر اصل مسئلہ کو بڑھائیں تا کہ دو بھائیوں پر تقسیم ہو سکے۔ مثلامیت نے بیوی اور دو بھائی چھوڑے اس لئے مسئلہ چار سے بنے گا۔ جس میں سے ایک چوتھائی بیوی کو دی جائے گی۔ اور تین چوتھائی بھائی کو بطور عصبہ دی جائے گی۔ چونکہ بھائی دو ہیں اس لئے تین اس پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ اس لئے دو کو اصل مسئلہ چار میں ضرب دو۔ جس سے اصل مسئلہ آٹھ ہو جائے گا۔ اور دونوں بھائیوں کو اس میں چھ ملیں گے اور ہر ایک بھائی کو تین تین مل جائیں گے۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔ میت 4 تصحیح بیوی 8 دو بھائی 3 1 6 2 تصحیح کے بعد بیوی کو ملا تصحیح کے بعد بھائیوں کو ملا ہر ایک بھائی کو ملا 4x2=8 ایک بھائی کو 3 ملیں گے۔ 1x2=2 3x2=6 6+2=3 تصحیح کا طریقہ
And if the problem divides among the heirs, then it is correct; but if the shares of a group among them do not divide upon them, then multiply their number into the base of the problem and its 'awl if it is 'awl. So whatever product results, from it the problem becomes correct. For example, a wife and two brothers. So the wife has one-fourth: one share; and for the two brothers is the residue: three shares, which do not divide upon them. So multiply two into the base of the problem, then it becomes eight. And from that the problem becomes correct. If the share that the group received divides upon their number, then there is no need to multiply into the base of the problem. For example, if they received two shares and there were two brothers, then there is no need to multiply into the base. But if they received three shares and there are two brothers, then two into three shares will be one and a half each, which is a fraction. So multiply the two brothers into the base to increase the base so that it can divide upon the two brothers. Example: The deceased left a wife and two brothers, so the problem is from four. Out of that, one-fourth is given to the wife, and three-fourths are given to the brothers as 'asabah. Since the brothers are two, three does not divide upon them. So multiply two into the base four, giving a base of eight. Then the brothers get six shares, and each brother gets three. The problem is as follows: Deceased 4, tashih: wife 8, two brothers 3, 1, 6, 2. After tashih, wife gets 2 (1x2), brothers get 6 (3x2), each brother gets 3 (6/2). The method of tashih.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on tashih (correction) of the inheritance base when the shares of a group of heirs do not divide evenly among them. The author gives the rule: if a group's total shares are not evenly divisible by the number of individuals in that group, multiply the number of individuals by the original base (including any 'awl) to get a new base from which every heir receives an integer number of shares. The Urdu commentary illustrates with a simple example: a wife, who gets 1/4 (1 share from base 4), and two brothers, who get the residue of 3 shares as 'asabah. Since 3 does not divide by 2, we multiply the number of brothers (2) by the base (4), obtaining a new base of 8. Now the wife gets 2 shares (1x2), and the brothers get 6 shares (3x2), each brother taking 3 shares. This is a fundamental principle in 'ilm al-fara'id known as tashih. The teacher should note that this rule applies to all groups, not just brothers.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tashih): Correction of the inheritance base by multiplying with the number of heirs in a group to obtain integer shares
عصبة (‘asabah): Residuary heir who inherits the remaining estate after fixed shares; here, the brothers take the residue as 'asabah
فريق (fariq): A group of heirs sharing the same category (e.g., two brothers, three sons)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased leaves a wife and two full brothers. The original base is 4. Why is tashih necessary?
A) Because the wife's share is 1/4, a fraction
B) Because the two brothers receive 3 shares as residue, which does not divide evenly by 2
C) Because the deceased also left a father
D) Because the estate is less than the total shares

Key Takeaway
When a group's total shares do not divide evenly by the number of individuals in that group, multiply the base by that number to correct the distribution.

Correction of Fractions in Inheritance (Tas-hih)
Rule for adjusting inheritance base when shares of a group cannot divide evenly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tas-hih to adjust the base number when the shares of a group of heirs are not evenly divisible among them.

Core Idea
Multiply the base by the number of heirs in the indivisible group to eliminate fractions.

In inheritance calculations, after assigning shares from the original base, we may find that a group of heirs (e.g., two brothers) receives a total number of shares that does not divide evenly among them. This lesson presents the Hanafi rule for correction (tas-hih): multiply the original base (or the 'awl-adjusted base) by the number of heirs in that group. The product becomes the new corrected base, ensuring each heir receives an integer number of shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original base number
Determine asl al-mas'alah from the denominators of the Quranic shares (e.g., wife's share 1/4 → base 4).
2
Assign shares as fractions of the base
Calculate each heir's portion: wife takes 1 share, residue (3 shares) goes to the brothers.
3
Check divisibility within each group
Total shares of the brothers = 3. Does 3 divide evenly by the number of brothers (2)? No.
Only check groups that receive a shared residue.
4
Apply tas-hih: multiply base by the number of heirs in the indivisible group
Multiply the original base (4) by the number of brothers (2) → new base = 8.
If the base had been increased by 'awl, use that 'awl-adjusted base instead.
5
Recompute shares under the corrected base
Wife: 1 × 2 = 2 shares; Brothers: 3 × 2 = 6 shares → each brother gets 3 shares.
The new base is 8; all shares are integers.

Source Text

Then what results, from that the problem becomes correct. Commentary
This passage states the rule for correcting fractional inheritance distributions (tas-hih). The author, Al-Sameri, explains that if the shares of a group of heirs (such as two brothers) do not divide evenly among them, we multiply the number of heirs in that group by the original base number (asl al-mas'alah). If the base was increased due to 'awl (proportional increase), we use the increased base. The product becomes the new corrected base. The example: a wife (share 1/4) and two brothers (residue 3/4). The original base is 4, giving wife 1 share and brothers 3 shares. Since 3 does not divide evenly between two brothers, we multiply the base (4) by the number of brothers (2) to get 8. Then wife gets 2 shares, each brother gets 3 shares. This method ensures each heir receives a whole number of shares without fractions in the calculation.

Key Terms
المسئلة (al-mas'alah): The inheritance problem or calculation; refers to the set of heirs and shares to be distributed.
تصحيح (tas-hih): The process of multiplying the base number to eliminate fractions where shares of a group of heirs do not divide evenly.
عول ('awl): The increase of the base number when the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the total; used to proportionally reduce all shares.

When a group of heirs receives a collective share that is not divisible by their number, multiply the base by that number to get a corrected base where all shares are integers.

Tabayun and Tashih in Inheritance Calculations
Explanation of tabayun rule with two faraid examples including 'awl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply tabayun (multiplication by number of heirs) to correct the faraid base when shares are not divisible, including cases with 'awl.

Core Idea
When a group of heirs' shares cannot be divided evenly, multiply the base by the number of heirs.

Inheritance calculations often leave shares that do not divide evenly among multiple heirs. The Hanafi method of tashih (correction) adjusts the base so every heir receives whole shares. This lesson focuses on tabayun—when the shares and the number of heirs are co-prime (no common factor), we multiply the original base by the number of heirs. We will work through two examples: a wife with two brothers (simple case) and a husband with three full sisters (involving 'awl).

Guided Path
1
Identify the group of heirs whose shares are not divisible
Look for the set of heirs whose collective share amount does not divide evenly among them. In the first example, two brothers receive 3 shares total; 3 is not divisible by 2. In the second, three sisters receive 4 shares; 4 not divisible by 3.
2
Check the relationship between number of heirs and shares
Determine if the number of heirs (n) and the share amount (s) are co-prime (tabayun) or share a common factor (tawafuq). If co-prime, you will multiply by n. If tawafuq, multiply by the party (n divided by common factor).
Co-prime means the greatest common divisor is 1.
3
Multiply the original base (asl al-mas'alah) by the number of heirs
For the first case, base = 4, multiplied by 2 (number of brothers) gives new base 8. For the second, after 'awl the base is 7, multiplied by 3 gives 21.
In the second case, 'awl already increased the base from 6 to 7.
4
Distribute the new shares proportionally
Each heir's share increases by the multiplication factor. Wife: 1 share → 2 shares (1/4 of new base). Brothers: 3 shares → 6 shares (each 3). Husband: 3 shares → 9 shares. Sisters: 4 shares → 12 shares (each 4).
The fractions remain the same, but expressed in a larger whole.
5
Verify and consider the calculator alternative
The classical method uses whole shares. Modern calculators can use decimal fractions (e.g., 100% total), which avoids tashih but loses the theoretical foundation of whole shares.
Classical Hanafi faraid requires whole shares for correctness.

Commentary
This passage introduces the rule of tabayun in inheritance calculations. When the shares allotted to a group of heirs cannot be divided evenly among them, we multiply the original base (asl al-mas'alah) by the number of heirs in that group. The first example is a wife and two brothers. The wife takes 1/4 (1 share out of base 4), and the two brothers take the remaining 3 shares. Since 3 is not divisible by 2, we multiply the base (4) by 2, giving a new base of 8. The wife now gets 2 shares, and the two brothers get 6 shares, each receiving 3. The commentator then shows a calculator method using decimal fractions, where the wife gets 25% and each brother 37.5% of 100. The second example involves 'awl (increase of the base): a husband and three full sisters. The husband's share is 1/2 (3/6), and the sisters' share is 2/3 (4/6), summing to 7/6, so the base increases from 6 to 7. The sisters' 4 shares are not divisible by 3, so we apply tabayun again, multiplying the base (7) by 3 to get 21. The husband now gets 9 shares, and the sisters 12 shares total, each 4. The commentator also provides a decimal calculator method dividing 100 after 'awl at 116.66, with each share becoming 0.8571.

Key Terms
سهم (sahm): Share of inheritance assigned to an heir, usually expressed as a fraction of the base.
تصحیح (tashih): The process of adjusting the base denominator so that each heir receives a whole number of shares.
عول ('awl): Increase of the base denominator when the sum of fixed shares exceeds the original base.
تباین (tabayun): When two numbers have no common factor other than 1, e.g., 3 and 2.

Tawafuq: Adjusting Base When Shares and Heir Count Share a Common Factor
Faraid rule with example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the tawafuq rule to adjust the base number in a faraid case when shares and number of heirs share a common factor.

Core Idea
When shares and heirs share a common factor, multiply the base by the party of the number, not the full count.

In inheritance calculations, after assigning shares, we often need to adjust the base so each heir receives an integer share. The rule of tawafuq (congruence) tells us that when the number of heirs in a group and their total shares share a common divisor, we multiply the original base by the party of the number (the number divided by the common divisor). This lesson works through the classic example of a wife and six brothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify heirs and their shares
List all heirs and determine their prescribed shares. In this case: wife gets 1/4 (fard), six brothers collectively get 3/4 (asabah).
2
Set the initial base number
The base is the denominator that makes all shares integral. For wife's 1/4 and brothers' 3/4, base = 4. Wife gets 1 share, brothers get 3 shares.
3
Check for tawafuq between shares and number of heirs
Compare the total shares of the group (3) with the number of heirs in that group (6). Find the greatest common divisor (GCD). Here GCD(3,6)=3 > 1, so tawafuq exists.
4
Compute the party of the number (wafq al-‘adad)
Divide the number of heirs by the common divisor: 6 ÷ 3 = 2. This is the multiplier.
5
Multiply the base by the party
New base = original base × party = 4 × 2 = 8. Now reassign shares: wife gets 2 (1/4 of 8), brothers get 6 shares total, each brother gets 1 share.

The meaning of tawafuq is that a smaller number divides a larger number evenly, like three divides six into two equal parts. So between six and three there is tawafuq with two. The author said: if there is tawafuq between the number of recipients and their shares, then multiply the base of the case by that number of tawafuq, then the case becomes correct. The case will be formed like this: Deceased: 4 multiplied by 8. Wife: 1? Six brothers: 2? After correction: brothers got 6? After correction: wife got 2? 2x4=8. Each brother gets 1. Method of correction: 3x2=6, 1x2=2. In this case, the recipients were six brothers and the total shares were three, so between three and six there is tawafuq because three divides six twice. So the tawafuq number is two. Therefore, multiply the original base (4) by 2, resulting in 8. From that, the six brothers got 6, and each brother got 1. The calculator calculation will be: Deceased: 100, wife: 25, six brothers: 75, each brother gets 12.5. In the calculator calculation, 75 is divided by 6, giving 12.5 for each brother.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage explains the rule of tawafuq (congruence) in inheritance calculations. When the shares (saham) of a group of heirs and the number of heirs (a'dad) share a common factor, we do not multiply by the full number of heirs but by the party of the number (juz' al-‘adad), which is the number of heirs divided by the common divisor. The example is a wife and six brothers. The wife gets 1/4 of the base (4), so 1 share; the six brothers collectively get the remaining 3 shares as asabah. Here the shares (3) and the number of brothers (6) have a common divisor of 3 (since 3 divides both 3 and 6). Therefore, we take the party of the number: 6 ÷ 3 = 2, and multiply the original base (4) by 2, giving 8. Now the wife gets 2 shares, and the six brothers get 6 shares, each brother receiving 1 share. The commentator clarifies that tawafuq means a smaller number divides a larger one evenly (e.g., 3 divides 6 into 2). The Urdu also repeats part of the previous 'awl example's calculator method, but the main focus is the wife+six brothers case. The calculator method shows that out of 100, wife gets 25, brothers get 75, each brother 12.5.

Key Terms
توافق (tawafuq): Congruence: two numbers share a common divisor greater than 1, e.g., 3 and 6 have tawafuq with 3.
وفق عدد (wafq al-‘adad): The common divisor (or sometimes the result of dividing the number by the common divisor) used as multiplier.
ثاث عدد (thāth ‘adad): One-third of the number (6/3=2). Used as the multiplier in tawafuq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of a wife and six brothers, what is the multiplier applied to the original base (4) and why?
A) Multiply by 6 because there are six brothers.
B) Multiply by 2 because the shares (3) and number (6) share a common factor of 3, so we use the party of the number (6/3=2).
C) Multiply by 3 because the common factor is 3.
D) Multiply by 4 to match the wife's share.

Key Takeaway
In tawafuq, multiply the base by the party of the number (number ÷ common divisor) to make shares divisible.

The Rule of Tawafuq in Inheritance Correction (Tashih)
Explains rule for tawafuq (agreement) between shares and number of heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when tawafuq exists between shares and number of heirs, and apply the tashih procedure by multiplying the wafq into the base number.

Core Idea
When heirs' shares and their count share a factor, multiply the base by their common part to make distribution whole.

In inheritance calculations, after assigning fixed shares, we often have a group of heirs entitled to a residue that is not divisible by their number. Classical Hanafi scholars developed a systematic method called tashih (correction) using the concept of tawafuq (agreement). This passage explains the rule for tawafuq: if the shares and the number of heirs have a common divisor greater than 1, we multiply the original base (asl al-mas'alah) by the wafq (the number of heirs divided by the common divisor) to make the shares divisible among them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their shares
List all heirs and their prescribed shares. For example, wife gets 1/4, six brothers get the residue (3/4).
The residue shares are taken as a fraction of the base; here 3/4 corresponds to 3 shares out of 4.
2
Compute the base number (asl al-mas'alah)
Determine the least common multiple of the denominators of the fixed shares. For wife's 1/4, base = 4.
If multiple fixed shares, base is LCM of denominators.
3
Determine the number of shares for the residue group
Subtract fixed share from total (1). Here, residue shares = 3 (out of 4).
These 3 shares belong to the six brothers as a group.
4
Check divisibility and tawafuq
Check if the number of shares (3) divides evenly by the number of heirs (6). It does not. Then find if they share a common factor. 3 and 6 share factor 3, so tawafuq exists.
If they were coprime (tabayun), different rule applies.
5
Compute wafq and multiply base
The wafq is the number of heirs divided by the common factor: 6 ÷ 3 = 2. Multiply the original base (4) by this wafq: 4 × 2 = 8. This is the corrected base.
The wafq is always the part that makes the shares divisible.
6
Distribute the new shares
Wife's share: 1/4 of new base = 2 shares. Brothers' share: remain 6 shares, each brother gets 1.
Now shares are integers and divisible.

If their shares agree with their number, multiply the common factor of their number into the base of the problem, like a woman and six brothers: for the woman is one-fourth, and for the brothers are three shares that are not divisible among them, so multiply one-third of their number into the base of the problem, and from it the problem becomes correct.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage explains the rule of tawafuq (agreement/co-prime with a common factor) in inheritance calculations. When the number of heirs in a group and their shares share a common factor (i.e., they are not divisible evenly but have a common divisor greater than 1), we multiply the common factor (wafq) into the original base number (asl al-mas'alah) to make the shares divisible. The example: a wife (1/4) and six brothers (remaining 3/4, so 3 shares). The number of brothers is 6, shares are 3; they agree with a common factor of 3 (since 3 divides both 3 and 6). The common factor is 3, but the text says 'thuluth 'adadihim' meaning one-third of their number (2), which is the wafq. Actually, the wafq of 6 with 3 is 2 (since 6/3=2). So they multiply 2 into the base (4) to get 8. Then each brother gets 1 share (3 shares × 2 / 6 = 1). The Urdu commentary elaborates the method. A calculator example is given: if the estate is 100, wife gets 25, brothers get 75 total, each brother 12.5.

Key Terms
توافق (tawāfuq): Two numbers that share a common divisor greater than 1 (i.e., they are not coprime but have a common factor). In inheritance, refers to the relationship between the number of heirs and their shares when they have a common factor.
وفق (wafq): The number that results from dividing the larger number by the common factor. In tashih, it is the multiplier applied to the base when tawafuq exists.
تصحیح (taṣḥīḥ): The process of adjusting the base number (asl al-mas'alah) so that fractional shares become whole numbers and each heir receives an integer number of shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a wife and six brothers, the base number is 4. Why is it necessary to multiply by 2?
A) Because 6 is even
B) Because the brothers' shares (3) and their number (6) agree on a common factor of 3, so the wafq of 6 is 2
C) Because the wife's share is 1/4
D) Because the total shares must sum to 8

Key Takeaway
Tawafuq allows a proportional increase of the base to make shares divisible while preserving heir ratios, using the wafq as the multiplier.

The Four Numerical Relationships in Tashih
Defines the four numerical relationships for inheritance tashih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four numerical relationships (tamathul, tadakhul, tawafuq, tabayun) and apply the correct multiplier for each in inheritance tashih.

Core Idea
The correct multiplier in tashih depends on the numerical relationship between the heir groups.

Inheritance tashih requires adjusting the base number so that shares divide evenly. The adjustment multiplier is determined by the relationship between the numbers of heirs in different groups: equality, inclusion, agreement, or mutual exclusion. This lesson defines each relationship and shows how to calculate the multiplier.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two numbers
Determine the numbers of heirs (or shares) from two groups that need to be combined. Focus on their numerical values.
In tashih, these numbers are usually the number of heads in two heir groups or the number of shares after initial fractions.
2
Check for equality (tamathul)
If the two numbers are exactly equal, use tamathul. The multiplier is one of the numbers (any one).
Example: 4 and 4 → multiplier = 4.
3
Check for inclusion (tadakhul)
If one number divides the other without a remainder, it is tadakhul. The multiplier is the larger number.
Example: 4 and 12 → 12 is the multiplier, because 4 divides 12 exactly.
4
Check for agreement (tawafuq)
If the numbers share a common factor greater than 1, it is tawafuq. Find the common factor (wafq). Divide one number by the factor, then use that quotient as the multiplier.
Example: 8 and 10 share common factor 2. Divide 8 by 2 = 4, or 10 by 2 = 5; either quotient is multiplied into the base.
5
If none, mutual exclusion (tabayun)
If the numbers are coprime (no common factor), it is tabayun. Multiply the two numbers together, then multiply that product into the base.
Example: 9 and 10 → multiplier = 9 × 10 = 90.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تماثل (۲) تداخل (۳) توافق (۴) تائین کیا ہیں؟ اوپر کے مسئلے کو سمجھنے کے لئے ان چار محاورات کو سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔ تماثل، تداخل توافق اور تائین۔
(۱) تماثل : دو عدد ایک جیسے ہوں ان کو تماثل کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے چار اور چار کہ دونوں عدد ایک جیسے ہیں، دس، دس کہ دونوں عدد ایک جیسے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں کسی ایک عدد سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینا کافی ہوگا۔
(۲) تداخل : چھوٹا عدد بڑے عدد میں داخل ہو جائے ایک مرتبہ کے ساتھ ، چاہے دو مرتبہ کے ساتھ ، چاہے تین مرتبہ کے ساتھ ، جیسے ہیں اور چار۔ کیونکہ چار ہیں میں پانچ مرتبہ داخل ہوتا ہے۔ یا چار اور بارہ کہ چار بارہ میں تین مرتبہ داخل ہوتا ہے۔ تو ان دونوں میں تداخل کی نسبت ہوئی۔ اس کے بڑے عدد کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے سے تصحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ مثال مذکور میں بیس سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے سے تصیح ہو جائے گی۔
(۳) توافق : دو عدد کسی تیسرے عدد سے موافق ہو اس کو تو افق کہتے ہیں۔ مثلا آٹھ اور دس ہے۔ اس میں آٹھ دس میں داخل نہیں ہے لیکن دو کا عدد چار مرتبہ میں آٹھ کو فنا کرتا ہے اور پانچ مرتبہ میں دس کو فنا کرتا ہے۔ تو چونکہ دو نے دس اور آٹھ دونوں کو فنا کیا اس لئے دو کا عدد توافق کے لئے ہوا۔ اور آٹھ اور دس میں تو افق کی نسبت ہوئی۔ اس میں جو تو افق کا عدد ہے جیسے مثال مذکور میں دو، اس سے فنا شدہ عدد کو ضرب دے کر جو ما حصل ہو اس سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے سے تصیح ہوگی۔
(۴) تباین : دو عددوں کے درمیان نہ توافق کی نسبت ہو اور نہ تداخل کی نسبت ہو اس کو تباہین کہتے ہیں۔ مثلا نو اور دس ، ان دونوں عددوں کو کوئی تیسر اعدد بھی نہیں کا تھا۔ اس لئے ان دونوں عددوں کے درمیان تبائین کی نسبت ہے۔ ان دونوں عددوں کو تبائین کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا طریقہ یہ ہوگا کہ دونوں عددوں کو ایک دوسرے سے ضرب دیں پھر حاصل ضرب کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دیں اس سے تصحیح ہوگی ۔ مثال مذکور میں نو ودس سے ضرب دیں تو نوے ہوئے۔ اب نوے سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دیں تو صحیح ہوگی۔
What are tamathul (2), tadakhul (3), tawafuq (4), and tabayun? It is necessary to understand these four terms to comprehend the above problem. Tamathul, tadakhul, tawafuq, and tabayun. (1) Tamathul: two numbers that are alike, e.g., 4 and 4, both numbers are alike; 10 and 10, both alike. In this case, multiplying either number into the base suffices. (2) Tadakhul: the smaller number enters into the larger number once, twice, or thrice, e.g., 5 and 20, because 4 enters 20 five times, or 4 and 12, because 4 enters 12 three times. So the relationship between them is tadakhul. Multiplying the larger number into the base corrects the problem. In the example, multiplying 20 into the base corrects it. (3) Tawafuq: two numbers agree with a third number, e.g., 8 and 10. Here 8 does not enter into 10, but the number 2 annihilates 8 four times and annihilates 10 five times. Since 2 annihilates both, 2 is the common factor. Then the relationship between 8 and 10 is tawafuq. Multiply the common factor into the base after dividing one of the numbers? Actually, multiply the quotient of one number divided by the common factor into the base. (4) Tabayun: when two numbers have neither tawafuq nor tadakhul, e.g., 9 and 10. No third number divides both. So between them is tabayun. Multiply both numbers together, then multiply the product into the base; the problem becomes correct. In the example, multiply 9 by 10 to get 90, then multiply 90 into the base.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage defines the four numerical relationships used in inheritance tashih (making shares divisible). Tamathul (equality): both numbers are equal, so multiply one into the base. Tadakhul (inclusion): one number is a multiple of the other, so multiply the larger into the base. Tawafuq (agreement): numbers share a common factor greater than 1, so multiply the wafq (the other number divided by the common factor) into the base. Tabayun (mutual exclusion): numbers are coprime, so multiply both together, then the product into the base. These relationships determine the multiplier to adjust the base number for proper division.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamāthul): Two numbers that are exactly equal.
تداخل (tadākhul): One number is a multiple of the other (the smaller divides the larger without remainder).
توافق (tawāfuq): Two numbers share a common divisor greater than 1 (they are not coprime).
تباین (tabāyun): Two numbers are coprime (no common divisor other than 1).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two numbers are 6 and 18, what is their relationship and what multiplier should be used for tashih?
A) Tamathul, multiplier = 6
B) Tadakhul, multiplier = 18
C) Tawafuq, multiplier = 3
D) Tabayun, multiplier = 108

Key Takeaway
The correct multiplier in tashih is determined by the numerical relationship between the two numbers: tamathul (use one), tadakhul (use larger), tawafuq (use wafq), tabayun (use product).

Rule for Multiple Groups with Tabayun
Explains the tabayun rule for tashih with multiple groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the tabayun rule to calculate the tashih multiplier when multiple groups of heirs have pairwise coprime head counts.

Core Idea
When heir counts are pairwise coprime, multiply them all to adjust the base.

This lesson addresses a common situation in inheritance distribution (faraid) where the numbers of heirs in different groups are all coprime to each other (tabayun). The rule provides a straightforward method to correct the base number so that each individual heir receives an integer share. You will learn to identify tabayun and apply the sequential multiplication method.

Guided Path
1
Identify groups and their shares
List each group of heirs (e.g., wives, grandmothers, brothers) and their fixed fractional shares from the Quran or residue.
Fixed shares: 1/4 for wives, 1/6 for grandmothers, residue for brothers.
2
Compute the base number (asl al-mas'alah)
Find the least common multiple (LCM) of the denominators of the fixed shares.
For 1/4 and 1/6, LCM is 12.
3
Assign shares to groups from the base
Compute each group's share count from the base: 1/4 of 12 = 3 for wives, 1/6 = 2 for grandmothers, residue = 12 - 3 - 2 = 7 for brothers.
These are total shares for the group, not per individual.
4
Check divisibility by the number of heads
For each group, divide the group's shares by the number of individuals. If any result is not an integer, tashih (adjustment) is required.
Wives: 3/2 = 1.5, grandmothers: 2/3 ≈ 0.666, brothers: 7/5 = 1.4. Tashih needed.
5
Apply the tabayun rule
If the numbers of heads in all groups are pairwise coprime (tabayun), multiply all these numbers together. Then multiply the product by the original base.
Heads: 2,3,5 are coprime. Multiply: 2×3×5 = 30. New base = 12×30 = 360.

Source Text

اگر تقسیم نہ ہوں دو فریق یا اس سے زیادہ کے سہام میں تو ضرب دے ایک فریق کے عدد کو دوسرے میں ۔ پھر حاصل ضرب کو ضرب دے تیسرے فریق کے عدد میں پھر حاصل ضرب کو اصل مسئلہ میں۔ حصہ لینے والے کئی فریق ہوں۔ اور ہر ایک فریق کی تعداد کچھ ایسی ہو کہ حصہ لینے والوں کی تعداد میں اور ان کے حصوں کے درمیان تبائین ہو۔ نہ چھوٹا عدد بڑے عدد میں داخل ہوتا ہو اور نہ توافق کے طور پر کوئی تیسر ا عدد دونوں کو کا تایا فتا کرتا ہو۔ ایسی صورت میں تمام عددوں کو ایک دوسرے سے ضرب دیں گے اور حاصل ضرب کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دیا جائے گا۔ جس سے صحیح ہوگی۔ مثلا میت نے دو بیویاں، تین دادیاں اور پانچ بھائی چھوڑے اس لئے مسئلہ بارہ سے چلے گا۔
If the shares of two or more factions do not divide, then multiply the number of one faction into the other, then multiply the product into the number of the third faction, then multiply the product into the base of the problem. When there are several factions, and the number of each faction and their shares are in tabayun (mutually exclusive) – neither does a smaller number enter into a larger one, nor does a third number annihilate both in the manner of tawafuq – then multiply all the numbers into each other, then multiply the product into the base of the problem. Thus it becomes correct. For example, the deceased left two wives, three grandmothers, and five brothers, so the problem proceeds from twelve.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where there are multiple groups of heirs (fariqayn or more), and within each group, the number of heirs and their shares are in tabayun (coprime) – meaning neither tadakhul nor tawafuq applies. In such a case, we multiply the numbers of all groups together (sequentially) and then multiply that product into the original base number of the problem. The example: two wives (2), three grandmothers (3), and five brothers (5). These numbers are all pairwise coprime? Check: 2 and 3 are coprime, 2 and 5 coprime, 3 and 5 coprime. So they are in tabayun. Multiply 2×3×5 = 30. Then multiply 30 into the base, which is 12 (the base for this example), giving 360. The shares would be assigned accordingly. The text cuts off, but the method is clear.

Key Terms
تباین (tabāyun): Two or more numbers that are pairwise coprime (no common divisor other than 1).

A) Because 30 is the LCM of 2, 3, and 5
B) Because the numbers 2, 3, and 5 are coprime, so they are multiplied together
C) Because 30 is the base number
D) Because the total shares sum to 30

Key Takeaway
When multiple heir groups have coprime head counts, multiply all those head counts together and multiply the product into the base number to achieve correct distribution.

Correcting Inheritance Shares: The Four Relationships and Their Application
Explains four proportional relationships for correcting share distribution in inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify tamathul, tadakhul, tawafuq, and tabayun between two numbers, and apply the correct procedure to calculate the tashih multiplier when shares are not divisible among multiple groups of heirs.

Core Idea
When shares don't divide evenly among heirs, multiply head counts using the correct relationship: equal, interlocking, agreeing, or disparate.

In inheritance calculations, we often encounter a situation where the number of shares assigned to a group of heirs (e.g., wives) is not divisible by the number of individuals in that group. To avoid fractional shares, we must find a multiplier that makes all shares whole numbers. The Hanafi school uses four simple arithmetic relationships—tamathul, tadakhul, tawafuq, and tabayun—to determine the correct multiplier. This lesson will teach you these relationships and how to apply them step by step using a classic example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب حساب الفرائض
وستة اخوة للمرأة الربع وللاخوة ثلثه اسهم لا تنقسم عليهم فاضرب ثلث عددهم في اصل المسألة ومنها تصح ۳۲۲۲ (۱۰) فان لم تنقسم سهام فريقين او اكثر فاضرب تماثل (۲) تداخل (۳) توافق (۴) تائین کیا ہیں؟ اوپر کے مسئلے کو سمجھنے کے لئے ان چار محاورات کو سمجھنا ضروری ہے۔ تماثل، تداخل توافق اور تائین۔ (۱) تماثل : دو عدد ایک جیسے ہوں ان کو تماثل کہتے ہیں۔ جیسے چار اور چار کہ دونوں عدد ایک جیسے ہیں، دس، دس کہ دونوں عدد ایک جیسے ہیں۔ اس صورت میں کسی ایک عدد سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینا کافی ہوگا۔ (۲) تداخل : چھوٹا عدد بڑے عدد میں داخل ہو جائے ایک مرتبہ کے ساتھ ، چاہے دو مرتبہ کے ساتھ ، چاہے تین مرتبہ کے ساتھ ، جیسے ہیں اور چار۔ کیونکہ چار ہیں میں پانچ مرتبہ داخل ہوتا ہے۔ یا چار اور بارہ کہ چار بارہ میں تین مرتبہ داخل ہوتا ہے۔ تو ان دونوں میں تداخل کی نسبت ہوئی۔ اس کے بڑے عدد کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے سے تصحیح ہو جائے گی ۔ مثال مذکور میں بیس سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے سے تصیح ہو جائے گی۔ (۳) توافق : دو عدد کسی تیسرے عدد سے موافق ہو اس کو تو افق کہتے ہیں۔ مثلا آٹھ اور دس ہے۔ اس میں آٹھ دس میں داخل نہیں ہے لیکن دوکا عدد چار مرتبہ میں آٹھ کو فنا کرتا ہے اور پانچ مرتبہ میں دس کو فنا کرتا ہے۔ تو چونکہ دو نے دس اور آٹھ دونوں کو فنا کیا اس لئے دو کا عدد توافق کے لئے ہوا۔ اور آٹھ اور دس میں تو افق کی نسبت ہوئی۔ اس میں جو تو افق کا عدد ہے جیسے مثال مذکور میں دو، اس سے فنا شدہ عدد کو ضرب دے کر جو ما حصل ہو اس سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دینے سے تصیح ہوگی۔ (۴) تباین : دو عددوں کے درمیان نہ توافق کی نسبت ہو اور نہ تداخل کی نسبت ہو اس کو تباہین کہتے ہیں۔ مثلا نو اور دس ، ان دونوں عددوں کو کوئی تیسر اعدد بھی نہیں کا تھا۔ اس لئے ان دونوں عددوں کے درمیان تبائین کی نسبت ہے۔ ان دونوں عددوں کو تبائین کہتے ہیں۔ اس کا طریقہ یہ ہوگا کہ دونوں عددوں کو ایک دوسرے سے ضرب دیں پھر حاصل ضرب کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دیں اس سے تصحیح ہوگی ۔ مثال مذکور میں نو ودس سے ضرب دیں تو نوے ہوئے۔ اب نوے سے اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دیں تو صحیح ہوگی۔ ۳۲۶۲ (۱۰) اگر تقسیم نہ ہوں دو فریق یا اس سے زیادہ کے سہام میں تو ضرب دے ایک فریق کے عدد کو دوسرے میں ۔ پھر حاصل ضرب کو ضرب دے تیسرے فریق کے عدد میں پھر حاصل ضرب کو اصل مسئلہ میں۔ حصہ لینے والے کئی فریق ہوں۔ اور ہر ایک فریق کی تعداد کچھ ایسی ہو کہ حصہ لینے والوں کی تعداد میں اور ان کے حصوں کے درمیان تبائین ہو۔ نہ چھوٹا عدد بڑے عدد میں داخل ہوتا ہو اور نہ توافق کے طور پر کوئی تیسر ا عدد دونوں کو کا تایا فتا کرتا ہو۔ ایسی صورت میں تمام عددوں کو ایک دوسرے سے ضرب دیں گے اور حاصل ضرب کو اصل مسئلہ میں ضرب دیا جائے گا۔ جس سے صحیح ہوگی۔ مثلا میت نے دو بیویاں، تین دادیاں اور پانچ بھائی چھوڑے اس لئے مسئلہ بارہ سے چلے گا۔

یہ مسئلہ بارہ سے چلایا۔ اس لئے دو بیویوں کو بارہ کی چوتھائی تین دیا۔ تین دادیوں کو بارہ کا چھٹا حصہ دو دیا۔ اور باقی سات حصیپانچ بھائیوں کو بطور عصہ دیا۔ دو بیویوں میں تین حصے تقسیم نہیں ہو سکے کیونکہ اس صورت میں کسر لازم آئے گا یعنی ڈیڑھ ڈیڑھ ہوگا۔ پھر دو اور تین میں تو افق یا تداخل نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ تائین کی نسبت ہے۔ تین دادیوں کو دو حصے ملے جو ان پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتے ، پھر تین اور دو کے درمیان تباین ہے۔ پانچ بھائیوں کو سات حصے ملے جوان پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتے کیونکہ سر لازم آئے گا۔ پھر پانچ اور سات میں تبائین کی نسبت ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ عد دروس دو، تین اور پانچ کے درمیان بھی تباہین ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ کو تین میں ضرب دیں پندرہ ہوگا ، پھر پندرہ کو دو میں ضرب دیں تو تمہیں ہوگا۔ اور تمیں کو اصل مسئلہ بارہ میں ضرب دیں تو تین سو ساٹھ ہوگا ۔ اس لئے تصحیح تین سو ساٹھ سے ہوگی۔ ہر ایک حصے داروں کو حصہ کس طرح دیا جائے : چونکہ تمیں سے اصل مسئلہ بارہ میں ضرب دیا تھا اس لئے تھیں سے دو بیویوں کے حصے تین میں ضرب دیں تو نوے ہوں گے۔ یہ نوے دو بیویوں کو دیں اور ہر ایک بیوی کو پینتالیس ملیں گے۔ اس تیس سے تین دادیوں کے حصے دو ہیں ضرب دیں تو ساٹھ ہوں گے ۔ اس کو تین وادیوں پر تقسیم کریں تو ہر ایک دادی کو میں ہیں ملیں گے۔ اسی تمہیں سے پانچ بھائیوں کے حصے سات میں ضرب دیں تو دوسو دس ہوں گے۔ اس کو پانچ
Chapter on Calculation of Inheritances. And six brothers, for the wife one-fourth and for the brothers one-third? Shares not divisible by them, so multiply one-third of their number into the base of the problem and from it the correction becomes correct. If shares of two or more groups are not divisible, then multiply the number of one group into the other, then the product into the third group, then the product into the base of the problem. What are tamathul (2), tadakhul (3), tawafuq (4), tabayun? To understand the above problem, it is necessary to understand these four relationships: tamathul, tadakhul, tawafuq, and tabayun. (1) Tamathul: Two numbers are equal; they are called tamathul. Like four and four, both numbers are the same; ten and ten, both numbers are the same. In this case, multiplying any one number into the base of the problem is sufficient. (2) Tadakhul: The smaller number enters into the larger number one time, or two times, or three times; like two and four? because four enters into two? five times; or four and twelve, because four enters into twelve three times. So between them there is tadakhul. By multiplying the larger number into the base of the problem, correction occurs. In the mentioned example, by multiplying twenty into the base of the problem, correction occurs. (3) Tawafuq: Two numbers agree with a third number; it is called tawafuq. For example, eight and ten. Here eight does not enter into ten, but the number two annihilates eight four times and annihilates ten five times. So because two annihilated both ten and eight, the number two became for tawafuq. And between eight and ten there is tawafuq. In this, the number of tawafuq, like two in the mentioned example, multiply the annihilated numbers? by it then multiply the product into the base of the problem for correction. (4) Tabayun: Between two numbers there is neither tawafuq nor tadakhul; it is called tabayun. For example, nine and ten; no third number annihilates both numbers. Therefore between them there is tabayun. The method is that multiply both numbers with each other, then multiply the product into the base of the problem; from this correction occurs. In the mentioned example, multiply nine and ten to get ninety; then multiply ninety into the base of the problem for correction. 3262 (10) If shares of two or more groups are not divisible, then multiply the number of one group into the other. Then multiply the product into the number of the third group. Then multiply the product into the base of the problem. When there are multiple groups of heirs, and the number of each group and their shares are such that there is tabayun between them, and the smaller number does not enter into the larger, and no third number annihilates both, then multiply all numbers with each other and then multiply the product into the base of the problem; thus correction occurs. For example, the deceased left two wives, three grandmothers, and five brothers. Therefore the base is twelve. The form of the problem will be: Deceased: 12, correction: 360. 2 wives: 5x3x2=30x12=360. 3 grandmothers: 5 brothers: 7, 210, 2, 60, 3, 90. Each gets 45, each gets 20, each gets 42. After correction, the brothers got: 7x30=210, the grandmothers got: 3x30=90, the two wives got: 2x30=60? Actually: 7x30=210, 3x30=90, 2x30=60. Total 360. Method of correction. Method of division. 210÷5=42, 60÷3=20, 90÷2=45. Each brother got 42, each grandmother got 20, each wife got 45. This base was started from twelve. So the two wives were given one-fourth of twelve, three. The three grandmothers were given one-sixth of twelve, two. And the remaining seven shares were given to the five brothers as asabah. The three shares could not be divided among the two wives because a fraction would occur, i.e., one and a half each. There is no tawafuq or tadakhul between two and three, rather tabayun. The two shares given to the three grandmothers could not be divided among them, so between three and two there is tabayun. The seven shares given to the five brothers could not be divided among them because a fraction would occur, so between five and seven there is tabayun. Secondly, between the numbers two, three, and five there is also tabayun. Therefore multiply five into three, get fifteen; then multiply fifteen into two, get thirty; then multiply thirty into the base twelve, get three hundred sixty. So correction is with three hundred sixty. How to give each heir his share: Since we multiplied thirty into the base twelve, from thirty multiply the two wives' share three, get ninety, give these ninety to the two wives, and each wife gets forty-five. From this thirty, multiply the three grandmothers' shares two, get sixty, divide among the three grandmothers, each grandmother gets twenty. From the same thirty, multiply the five brothers' shares seven, get two hundred ten, divide among the five brothers, each gets forty-two.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is a detailed faraid (inheritance) lesson on correcting a problem when shares are not divisible among multiple groups of heirs. It begins by introducing the four key proportional relationships used in Hanafi inheritance calculations: tamathul (equality), tadakhul (interlocking), tawafuq (agreement), and tabayun (disparity). Tamathul is when two numbers are equal; then using either number as a multiplier suffices. Tadakhul is when a smaller number divides the larger number completely; then the larger number is used as the multiplier. Tawafuq is when two numbers share a common divisor; then the common divisor is used to reduce the numbers and the product is multiplied into the base. Tabayun is when they have no common divisor; then both numbers are multiplied together. The passage then applies these concepts to a concrete case: a deceased leaves two wives, three grandmothers (dadiyan), and five brothers. The base problem (asl al-mas'alah) is 12 because the shares are: wives get 1/4 = 3, grandmothers get 1/6 = 2, and the remaining 7 goes to the brothers as asabah. None of these shares divide evenly among the heads of the groups (2, 3, 5) because 3 is not divisible by 2, 2 is not divisible by 3, and 7 is not divisible by 5. Moreover, the numbers 2, 3, and 5 are in tabayun with each other. Therefore, according to the rule for multiple groups with tabayun, we multiply all the head counts: 2 × 3 × 5 = 30, then multiply 30 by the base 12 to get 360 as the corrected base. Then each group's share from the original base (3 for wives, 2 for grandmothers, 7 for brothers) is multiplied by the same factor 30 to get the new shares: wives 90, grandmothers 60, brothers 210. Finally, each heir's individual portion is found by dividing the group's new share by the number of heads in that group: each wife gets 90 ÷ 2 = 45, each grandmother gets 60 ÷ 3 = 20, each brother gets 210 ÷ 5 = 42. The commentary includes a table showing the multiplication steps. This entire process is known as tashih (correction) and is essential in faraid when shares do not divide evenly. The passage demonstrates a rigorous procedural method typical of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamāthul): Two numbers are equal; e.g., 4 and 4. In faraid, when the number of heads in a group equals the number of shares, use that number as the multiplier.
تداخل (tadākhul): The smaller number divides the larger number exactly. Example: 4 and 20. The larger number is used as the multiplier for correction.
توافق (tawāfuq): Two numbers share a common divisor greater than 1. Example: 8 and 10 share 2. Divide each by the common divisor and multiply the results.
تباین (tabāyun): Two numbers have no common divisor other than 1; they are coprime. Example: 9 and 10. Multiply them directly.
تصحیح (taṣḥīḥ): The process of adjusting the base denominator so that all shares can be divided among the heirs without fractions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example with 2 wives, 3 grandmothers, and 5 brothers, what is the relationship between the head counts 2 and 3?
A) Tamathul
B) Tadakhul
C) Tawafuq
D) Tabayun

Key Takeaway
To correct a faraid problem when shares are not divisible among multiple groups, identify the relationship between head counts and shares (tamathul, tadakhul, tawafuq, or tabayun) and apply the corresponding rule to find the smallest multiplier that makes all shares whole.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
10 min
Faraid Tashih with Tabayun: Two Wives, Three Grandmothers, Five Brothers
Detailed calculation of inheritance with correction (tashih) due to tabayun among groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance shares for a case with tabayun using the Hanafi tashih method, including identifying disparity and applying the correct multiplier.

Core Idea
When shares and heads in each group are mutually prime, multiply all head counts and adjust the base to distribute.

In this lesson, we examine a classic faraid case involving two wives, three grandmothers, and five brothers. The shares are simple (1/4, 1/6, residue), but the distribution requires a correction known as tashih because the number of individuals in each group does not evenly divide their assigned shares. You will learn how to detect tabayun (disparity) and apply the multiplication method to achieve integer shares for each heir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their prescribed shares
List all heirs: two wives (fard 1/4), three grandmothers (fard 1/6), five brothers (asabah, residue). Determine the base number (asl al-masalah) from the denominators: LCM of 4 and 6 is 12. Assign shares: wives 3 (1/4 of 12), grandmothers 2 (1/6 of 12), brothers 7 (residue 12 - 3 - 2).
The brothers take the remainder as asabah.
2
Detect tabayun (disparity) between heads and shares
For each group, compare the number of heads (individuals) with the share they collectively receive. Wives: 2 heads with 3 shares → 3/2 is not integer, and 2 and 3 have no common factor (GCD=1) → tabayun. Grandmothers: 3 heads with 2 shares → tabayun. Brothers: 5 heads with 7 shares → tabayun. Also, the head counts 2, 3, 5 are mutually prime (tabayun among themselves).
Tabayun means the two numbers are coprime (no common divisor other than 1). If there were a common factor (wafaq), we would use the wafq (common divisor) instead of the whole head count.
3
Apply the tashih multiplier
Since all groups have tabayun with their shares and the head counts are also mutually prime, multiply all head counts together: 2 × 3 × 5 = 30. This is the tashih multiplier. Multiply the original base (12) by 30 to get the corrected base (mujtama' al-sahih): 12 × 30 = 360.
If any group had wafaq (common factor) between its heads and shares, the multiplier would be the LCM of the head counts or the product after reducing by the wafq. Here, all are tabayun, so the product of heads is straightforward.
4
Multiply each group's share by the multiplier
For each group, multiply their original share (from base 12) by the tashih multiplier (30). Wives: 3 × 30 = 90; Grandmothers: 2 × 30 = 60; Brothers: 7 × 30 = 210. These are the total shares in the corrected base.
These numbers now sum to 360 (90+60+210).
5
Divide by the number of heads in each group
Divide each group's corrected total by its number of heads to get each individual's share. Wives: 90 ÷ 2 = 45 each; Grandmothers: 60 ÷ 3 = 20 each; Brothers: 210 ÷ 5 = 42 each. These are the final shares per person from the corrected base of 360.
Alternatively, you can express each heir's share as a fraction of the total estate: wives 45/360 = 1/8 each, grandmothers 20/360 = 1/18 each, brothers 42/360 = 7/60 each.

یہ مسئلہ بارہ سے چلایا۔ اس لئے دو بیویوں کو بارہ کی چوتھائی تین دیا۔ تین دادیوں کو بارہ کا چھٹا حصہ دو دیا۔ اور باقی سات حصے پانچ بھائیوں کو بطور عصہ دیا۔ دو بیویوں میں تین حصے تقسیم نہیں ہو سکے کیونکہ اس صورت میں کسر لازم آئے گا یعنی ڈیڑھ ڈیڑھ ہوگا۔ پھر دو اور تین میں تو وفاق یا تداخل نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ تباین کی نسبت ہے۔
تین دادیوں کو دو حصے ملے جو ان پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتے، پھر تین اور دو کے درمیان تباین ہے۔
پانچ بھائیوں کو سات حصے ملے جو ان پر تقسیم نہیں ہو سکتے کیونکہ کسر لازم آئے گا۔ پھر پانچ اور سات میں تباین کی نسبت ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ اعداد رؤوس دو، تین اور پانچ کے درمیان بھی تباین ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ کو تین میں ضرب دیں پندرہ ہوگا، پھر پندرہ کو دو میں ضرب دیں تو تیس ہوگا۔ اور تیس کو اصل مسئلہ بارہ میں ضرب دیں تو تین سو ساٹھ ہوگا۔ اس لئے تصحیح تین سو ساٹھ سے ہوگی۔ ہر ایک حصے داروں کو حصہ کس طرح دیا جائے: چونکہ تیس سے اصل مسئلہ بارہ میں ضرب دیا تھا اس لئے تیس سے دو بیویوں کے حصے تین میں ضرب دیں تو نوے ہوں گے۔ یہ نوے دو بیویوں کو دیں اور ہر ایک بیوی کو پینتالیس ملیں گے۔ اس تیس سے تین دادیوں کے حصے دو میں ضرب دیں تو ساٹھ ہوں گے۔ اس کو تین دادیوں پر تقسیم کریں تو ہر ایک دادی کو بیس ملیں گے۔ اسی تیس سے پانچ بھائیوں کے حصے سات میں ضرب دیں تو دو سو دس ہوں گے۔ اس کو پانچ بھائیوں پر تقسیم کریں تو ہر ایک بھائی کو بیالیس ملیں گے۔

اس حساب میں کسی فریق کے حصے داروں کو ضرب دینے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کلکولیٹر پوائنٹ ناپتا ہے اس لئے کسر اور پوائنٹ سے تقسیم کر دیں۔ ہر ایک حصے دار کو پوائنٹ کے حساب سے حصہ مل جائے گا۔ مثلا ہر بیوی کو ساڑھے بارہ ملا تو 12.5 لکھ دیا۔ یعنی سو روپیہ میت کی میراث ہے تو اس میں سے ایک بیوی کو 12.5 یعنی ساڑھے بارہ روپیے ملیں گے۔ اسی پر آگے قیاس کر لیں۔
و یہ تباین کی مثال ہے۔
The form of the case will be like this. Deceased: base 12, correction 360. 2 wives (5x3x2=30x12 =360). 3 grandmothers. 5 brothers. 7, 210; 2, 60; 3, 90. Each gets 45, each gets 20, each gets 42. After correction, given to 5 brothers: 7x30=210. After correction, given to 3 grandmothers: 2x30=60. After correction, given to two wives: 3x30=90. Method of correction: 210÷5=42, 60÷3=20, 90÷2=45. Each brother got 42, each grandmother got 20, each wife got 45. This case was run from 12. So two wives were given three, a quarter of twelve. Three grandmothers were given two, a sixth of twelve. And the remaining seven shares were given to five brothers as asabah. The three shares could not be divided among the two wives because in that case a fraction would arise, i.e., one and a half each. Then between two and three there is no agreement (wafaq) or inclusion (tadakhul), but rather disparity (tabayun). Two shares were given to three grandmothers which could not be divided among them; then between three and two there is disparity. Seven shares were given to five brothers which could not be divided among them because a fraction would arise; then between five and seven there is disparity. The second point is that the numbers of heads (a'dad al-ru'us) two, three, and five are also disparate. So multiply five by three to get fifteen, then multiply fifteen by two to get thirty, and multiply thirty by the original base twelve to get three hundred sixty. Therefore the correction is from three hundred sixty. How to give shares to each shareholder: Since we multiplied the original base twelve by thirty, multiply the shares of the two wives (three) by thirty to get ninety. Give this ninety to the two wives, and each wife gets forty-five. Multiply the shares of the three grandmothers (two) by thirty to get sixty. Divide this among the three grandmothers, each grandmother gets twenty. Multiply the shares of the five brothers (seven) by thirty to get two hundred ten. Divide this among the five brothers, each brother gets forty-two. The calculator's calculation will be like this. Deceased: 100. 2 wives: 58.34, 16.66, 25. Each gets 12.5, each gets 5.55, each gets 11.66. After division, each brother gets 58.34÷5=11.66. Method of division: after division, grandmother got 16.66÷3=5.55, wife got 25÷2=12.50. In this calculation, there is no need to multiply the shares of any party because the calculator handles decimal points, so divide with fractions and decimals. Each shareholder gets their share according to the decimal. For example, each wife got twelve and a half, so write 12.5. That is, if the deceased's inheritance is one hundred rupees, then one wife gets 12.5, i.e., twelve and a half rupees. Apply analogy to the rest. And this is an example of tabayun.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is a detailed faraid case demonstrating the correction (tashih) of the base when there is tabayun (disparity) between the number of heads in each heir group and their shares. The heirs are two wives, three grandmothers (paternal or maternal?), and five brothers. The original base is 12: wives get 1/4 (3), grandmothers get 1/6 (2), brothers get the residue (7). However, 3 cannot divide evenly among 2 wives, 2 among 3 grandmothers, and 7 among 5 brothers. Since the numbers of heads (2,3,5) are mutually prime (tabayun), we multiply them: 2×3×5=30, then multiply the original base 12 by 30 to get 360. Then each group's original share is multiplied by 30, and then divided by the number of heads in that group. The result: each wife gets 45, each grandmother 20, each brother 42. The passage also includes a modern calculator method for the same case using decimal division, noting that calculators avoid the need for tashih. This example illustrates the principle of tashih in faraid when shares and heads are not divisible.

Key Terms
تصحیح (tashih): Correction of the base number to allow integer division among heirs within groups.
تباین (tabayun): Mutual disparity: two numbers have no common factor other than 1 (e.g., 2 and 3, 5 and 7).
عصہ (asabah): Residuary heir: takes the remainder after fixed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the given case, why was the base number multiplied by 30?
A) Because the total shares exceeded the base
B) Because the number of heads in each group were mutually prime (tabayun) with their shares
C) Because there was interference (tadakhul) between the groups
D) Because the calculator required integer division

Key Takeaway
When the shares assigned to a group of heirs cannot be divided evenly among their heads due to tabayun, tashih is applied by multiplying the base by the product of all head counts (or LCM if wafaq) to allow integer distribution.

Rule of Tamathul: Equal Numbers in Faraid Correction
Statement of rule with example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tamathul when correcting the base in a faraid case where two heir groups have equal head counts.

Core Idea
When head counts are equal, one number suffices—do not multiply both.

In faraid, after determining shares, the base number often needs correction (tashih) when shares cannot be divided evenly among heirs in a group. When two groups have the same number of heads, we apply the rule of tamathul: one number stands for the other. This lesson walks through the rule and its application with a concrete example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heir groups and their head counts
List each group of heirs with the same share. In the example: wives (2 heads) and brothers (2 heads). Note their head counts.
Wives share 1/4, brothers share residue as asabah.
2
Check for tamathul (equality)
Compare the head counts of the groups. If they are exactly equal, tamathul applies. Here both are 2.
If not equal, proceed to tawafuq or tabayun.
3
Use one head count as the multiplier
Multiply the original base (4) by the common head count (2) to get the corrected base (8).
You do not multiply both numbers; one suffices.
4
Distribute the adjusted shares
Multiply each group's share from the original base by the multiplier. Wives' share becomes 1×2=2, divided among 2 wives = 1 each. Brothers' share becomes 3×2=6, divided among 2 brothers = 3 each.
Ensure the total shares sum to the corrected base.
5
Verify the result
Check that each heir receives an integer share and that the distribution is correct.
If not an integer, further correction may be needed.

3263 (11) If the numbers are equal, one suffices for the other, like two wives and two brothers. Then multiply two into the original base. If the numbers are equal, then one of them is sufficient for the other. For example, two wives and two brothers. So multiply two into the original base. In this case, there are two wives and two brothers. Both have tamathul (equality), meaning both numbers are of the same type. Therefore, there is no need to multiply both into the original base; rather, multiplying only one number into the original base will make it correct. The case will be like this: Deceased: base 4, correction 8. 2×4=8. 2 wives, 2 brothers. Method of correction: 1×2=2, 3×2=6; 3, 6; 1, 2. Each gets 1, each gets 3. After correction, given to two wives, given to two brothers.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage states a rule in faraid correction (tashih): when two groups of heirs have the same number of heads (tamathul), you only need to use one of those numbers as a multiplier when correcting the base. The example is a case with two wives and two brothers. The original base is 4: wives get 1/4 (1 share) and brothers get the residue (3 shares). But 1 share cannot be divided among 2 wives, and 3 shares cannot be divided among 2 brothers. Both groups have head count 2. Since 2 and 2 are equal (tamathul), we use only one '2' as the multiplier. Multiply the base 4 by 2 to get 8. Then wives' share becomes 1×2=2, divided among 2 wives gives 1 each; brothers' share becomes 3×2=6, divided among 2 brothers gives 3 each. The key principle: when head counts are equal, one suffices for multiplication; you do not multiply both, which would be redundant.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamathul): Equality of numbers: two numbers are exactly the same (e.g., 2 and 2).
اجزأ (ajza'a): Suffices, is sufficient: one number stands in for the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Multiply the number of heads of both groups into the base
B) Multiply the number of heads of only one group into the base
C) Multiply the sum of the head counts into the base
D) No multiplication is needed because the numbers are equal

Key Takeaway
When head counts of two heir groups are equal, use only one as the multiplier in tashih.

Rules of Tamasul and Tabayun in Inheritance Calculations
Explains rules for equal and mutually prime numbers in inheritance calculations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply tamasul and tabayun rules to correct inheritance shares when multiple heirs share a category.

Core Idea
When heirs' numbers are equal or mutually prime, specific multiplication rules ensure whole-number shares.

In inheritance calculations, after assigning shares, we often face the problem that a share allocated to a group cannot be evenly divided among its members. This passage explains two key scenarios: when the numbers of two groups are equal (tamasul) and when they are mutually prime (tabayun). Mastering these rules speeds up the tashih process and avoids fractional shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify groups and their member counts
List each category of heirs and the number of individuals in each. For example, 2 wives and 2 brothers: both groups have 2 members.
The numbers determine which rule applies.
2
Check the relationship between numbers
Determine if the numbers are exactly equal (tamasul) or if they share no common divisor other than 1 (tabayun). For tamasul, e.g., 2 and 2. For tabayun, e.g., 2 and 3.
If numbers are equal, one suffices; if mutually prime, each must be handled separately.
3
Apply tamasul rule
If the numbers of two groups are equal, multiply the original base number by one of those numbers. Example: base 4 multiplied by 2 gives 8, making each wife get 1 share and each brother 3.
Only one multiplication is needed, not both.
4
Apply tabayun rule
If numbers of multiple groups are mutually prime (e.g., 2, 3, 5), multiply the original base by the product of these numbers. For example, base 12 multiplied by 30 (2×3×5) gives 360, allowing integer division.
The source also shows using a calculator to avoid multiplication, but the classical method uses multiplication.

Divide on the brothers, then each brother will get 42 each. The calculator's calculation will be as follows: Deceased 100, 2 wives, 3 grandmothers, 5 brothers, 58.34, 16.66, 25 each gets 12.5, each gets 5.55, each gets 11.66. In this calculation, there is no need to multiply any party's shares because the calculator knows the decimal point, so divide by fractions and decimal points. Each heir will get a share according to the decimal. For example, each wife got 12 and a half, so write 12.5. That is, if the deceased left 100 rupees, one wife gets 12.5 rupees. Analogize from this. Therefore, it is not necessary to multiply both in the original problem; rather, multiplying by only one number in the original problem will make it correct. The problem will be: Deceased 4, correct 8; 2x4=8; 2 wives; 2 brothers. Method of tashih: 1x2=2, 3x2=6, 3, 6, 1, 2; each gets 1, each gets 3; After tashih: two wives got: 2; two brothers got: 6.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage explains two fundamental rules for correcting inheritance shares when the numbers of heirs in different categories cannot evenly divide the assigned shares. The first rule is tamasul (equality): when the numbers of two groups of heirs are equal, multiplying one of those numbers into the original base suffices to make all shares whole. For example, with two wives and two brothers, the original base is 4 (wives get 1 share, brothers get 3 shares). Since the 1 share cannot be split among 2 wives and the 3 shares cannot be split among 2 brothers, we multiply the base by 2 (the number of either group) to get 8, making each wife get 1 share and each brother get 3 shares. The second rule is tabayun (mutual primeness): when the numbers of two groups have no common divisor (e.g., 2 wives, 3 grandmothers, 5 brothers), the text shows we can avoid multiplying altogether by using a calculator and dividing the shares directly as decimals. This is permissible because the calculator handles the fractions without needing to convert the base. The teacher emphasizes that when numbers are equal, only one multiplication is needed, saving effort.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamasul): Equality of numbers between two groups of heirs, e.g., both groups have 2 members each.
تباین (tabayun): Mutual primeness, meaning two numbers have no common divisor other than 1, e.g., 2 and 3.
تصحیح (tashih): Correction of the base number to allow whole number shares for each individual heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tamasul example with 2 wives and 2 brothers, what is the base number after tashih?
A) 4
B) 6
C) 8
D) 12

Key Takeaway
In inheritance corrections, equality (tamasul) requires multiplying by one number; mutual primeness (tabayun) requires multiplying by the product of the numbers.

Rule of Tadakhul in Inheritance Calculations
Explains the rule of tadakhul in inheritance calculations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of tadakhul to correct the base number in a Hanafi inheritance calculation when the number of heirs in one group is a divisor of another group.

Core Idea
When the number of one heir group divides the other, multiply the larger number into the base—the smaller is already covered.

In Hanafi inheritance calculations, after assigning shares, the base number often requires correction (tashih) to allow equal distribution. When the count of one heir group is a divisor of another, the rule of tadakhul applies: only the larger number needs to be multiplied into the base. This lesson explores the example of four wives and two brothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify Heirs and Their Shares
List all heirs and their prescribed shares. For 4 wives and 2 brothers, wives receive 1/4 (fard) and brothers get the residue (asabah).
Wives share equally in their 1/4; brothers share equally in the remaining 3/4.
2
Set the Original Base Number
The base is the denominator of the fractional shares. Here, base = 4. Wives get 1 portion, brothers get 3 portions.
3
Check Divisibility of Portions by Heir Count
The wives' 1 portion cannot be divided among 4 wives; the brothers' 3 portions cannot be divided among 2 brothers. Correction is needed.
If portions divided evenly, no tashih required.
4
Recognize Tadakhul Relationship
The number of brothers (2) divides the number of wives (4) exactly. This is tadakhul: the smaller is a part of the larger.
Tadakhul is one of the four relationships: tamathul, tabayun, tawafuq, tadakhul.
5
Multiply the Base by the Larger Number
Multiply the original base (4) by the larger number (4) to get the new base (16). This single multiplication suffices for both groups.
If the relationship were tabayun (no common divisor), you would multiply both numbers.

Al-Sharh al-Thamiri Volume 4 466 Chapter of Calculation of Inheritances. 3264 (12) And if one of the two numbers is a part of the other, the larger suffices. After division, one wife got [and] one brother got: 2÷2=1, 6÷2=3. Division method. In this problem, two wives got one share which cannot be divided among two, similarly two brothers got three shares which cannot be divided among two brothers. But both have two, so multiply the original problem of four by one number, i.e., two, and it becomes eight. The calculator's calculation will be: Deceased 100, 2 wives, 2 brothers, 25, 75; each gets 12.5, each gets 37.5. Since the calculator knows the decimal point, so the two wives got 25, then halved it, so each wife got 12.5. Similarly, the two brothers got 75, then halved it, so each brother got 37.5. This is an example of tamasul. 3264 (12) If one of the two numbers is a part of the other, then the larger number makes the smaller needless, like four wives and two brothers. When you multiply by four, it suffices for two. This is an example of tadakhul. In this problem, four is the larger number and two is the smaller number, and two is inside four twice. Therefore, multiplying the original problem by the larger number also suffices for the smaller number. Through this tashih is achieved. The problem will be: Deceased 4, tashih 16; 4 wives; 4x4=16; 2 brothers; 1, 4, 3, 12; each gets 1, each gets 6. After tashih: two brothers got: 12; four wives got: 4. 3x4=12, 1x4=4. The method of tashih.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage explains the rule of tadakhul (one number being a part of the other). In inheritance calculation, when the number of one group of heirs is a divisor of the number of another group, you only need to multiply the larger number into the base. The text gives two examples. The first example (confusingly labeled 'tamasul' but actually a tabayun case with 2 wives and 2 brothers) shows a calculator approach that bypasses multiplication. The second example explicitly illustrates tadakhul: 4 wives and 2 brothers. Here, the original base is 4 (wives get 1 share, brothers get 3 shares). But 1 cannot be divided among 4 wives, and 3 cannot be divided among 2 brothers. Since the number of wives (4) is a multiple of the number of brothers (2), we multiply the base by the larger number (4) to get 16. After correction, each wife gets 1 share and each brother gets 6 shares. The teacher emphasizes that tadakhul simplifies the process: only one multiplication by the larger number is needed.

Key Terms
تداخل (tadakhul): One number being a part or divisor of the other, e.g., 2 is a part of 4.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tadakhul example with 4 wives and 2 brothers, what is the base number after tashih?
A) 4
B) 8
C) 12
D) 16

Key Takeaway
The rule of tadakhul simplifies inheritance corrections: multiply only by the larger number when it is a multiple of the smaller.

Tamāthal and Tadākhul in Inheritance Calculations
Explains tamāthal and tadākhul rules for base correction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply tamāthal and tadākhul to correct the base number in inheritance problems when shares are not divisible among heirs.

Core Idea
When shares cannot divide evenly, multiply by the common number of heads — but check for tamāthal or tadākhul shortcuts.

In inheritance distribution, we often encounter cases where the shares allocated to a category of heirs cannot be divided equally among them. For example, two wives cannot split one share. The solution is taṣḥīḥ (correction) of the base number. This lesson introduces two simplified rules—tamāthal (equality) and tadākhul (interlocking)—that determine the multiplier without trial and error.

Guided Path
1
Identify Heirs and Their Shares
List all heirs, determine their fard (Quranic) shares, and the residual asabah. Compute the base number (asl al-masalah) from the denominators.
For the tamāthal example: 2 wives (1/4 share) and 2 brothers (3/4 residual). Base = 4.
2
Check Divisibility of Each Share Category
Divide the total shares of each category by the number of heads in that category. If any division leaves a fraction, taṣḥīḥ is required.
1 share for 2 wives: not divisible. 3 shares for 2 brothers: not divisible.
3
Determine the Relationship Between Numbers of Heads
Compare the number of heads in the categories that have remainder problems. The relationship can be tamāthal (equal), tadākhul (one is part of the other), tawāfuq (common factor), or tabāyun (no common factor).
Here both categories have 2 heads, so tamāthal: the numbers are equal.
4
Apply the Appropriate Multiplier for Taṣḥīḥ
For tamāthal, multiply the base by that common number. For tadākhul, multiply by the larger number. For tawāfuq, multiply by the common factor. For tabāyun, multiply by the product of the numbers.
For tamāthal: multiplier = 2. New base = 4 × 2 = 8.
5
Compute Final Shares
Multiply each category's original share by the multiplier to get new shares, then divide by the number of heads.
Wives: 1×2=2, each gets 1. Brothers: 3×2=6, each gets 3. Whole estate = 8 shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
